On 15:22:45 Apr 01, radha krishnan wrote:
> My requirement of using perl expect I want to communicate through
> minicom.In which am able to login , when i execute the commands it is not
> wriiting into the file in the required format , it mostly writes in the
> binary format. Can anyone tell that is there a way / module in perl

I get this

http://search.cpan.org/search?query=minicom&mode=all

but I have not spent much time on it.

There may be a speed setting problem in minicom or you might be using
hardware flow control.

Inside minicom type Ctrl-A O and fix those problems.

Minicom itself can log commands I think.

You can also use an interactive command like tip(1) or cu(1) for this
purpose.

Best of luck.

-Girish

Subject: [Ilugc] Q: Who Really Creates Linux? A: The Enterprise

Hi,

http://www.linux-watch.com/news/NS6229131777.html

So, while Linux does have a substantial contribution being made to it by 
amateurs, the vast bulk of it is being written by corporate programmers. 
The companies that are building Linux, in order of their contributions 
to the kernel, are:

       1) Red Hat, 11.2 percent
       2) Novell, 8.9 percent
       3) IBM, 8.3 percent
       4) Intel, 4.1 percent
       5) LF, 3.5 percent
       6) SGI, 2.0 percent
       7) MIPS Technology, 1.6 percent
       8) Oracle, 1.3 percent
       9) MontaVista, 1.2 percent
       10) Lintronix, 1.0 percent.


In addition, consultants' efforts have counted for 2.5 percent of the 
total work on Linux.

Rahul

Microsoft wins battle for OOXML approval
http://news.zdnet.co.uk/software/0,1000000121,39378350,00.htm 


The International Organization for Standardization has officially
approved Microsoft's OOXML specification as a standard.

The news confirms documents leaked on Tuesday were genuine.
Three-quarters of the "Principal Countries" involved in the vote gave
their approval (at least two-thirds were needed) and just 14 percent of
participating members of ISO and the International Electrotechnical
Commission (IEC) disapproved (under a quarter was needed).

According to ISO's Wednesday statement: "Subject to there being no
formal appeals from ISO/IEC national bodies in the next two months, the
International Standard will accordingly proceed to publication."

Although there have been allegations of voting irregularities within
some of the national standards bodies that in turn participated in the
ISO vote, no national body has yet made a formal appeal to ISO.

One prominent example had been an objection from Steve Pepper, the
chairman of Standard Norge's joint technical committee, which he faxed
directly to the ISO. In the letter, he claimed that 80 percent of the
committee had been against the OOXML standard being passed ? Norway
officially recorded a vote of approval.

However, a spokesperson for Standard Norge told ZDNet.co.uk on Wednesday
that the organisation had not made a formal appeal to ISO, and did not
intend to do so. "One of the committee members sent a fax to ISO about
this matter, but he did that directly and not through us," the
spokesperson said.

A spokesperson for ISO confirmed on Wednesday that it had not yet
received any formal objections to the OOXML voting process, and refused
to comment on the reports of voting irregularities within national
bodies.

The dichotomy between working for "open source mentality" vs "money" is 
frequently a false one. Many people with a passion for Free software and 
money is a means to pursue that passion.

Rahul

From ashokece at yahoo.co.uk  Wed Apr  2 21:31:48 2008
From: ashokece at yahoo.co.uk (ashok sezhiyan)
Date: Wed Apr  2 21:32:21 2008
Subject: [Ilugc] vim undo search
Message-ID: <845043.80623.qm@web24214.mail.ird.yahoo.com>


> :nohlsearch - clears the current search highlight
> :set nohlsearch - permanently disables search highlight

If you find it difficult to type the above command, just map keys to do the job

* Press Space to turn off highlighting and blank message.
:noremap <silent> <Space> :silent noh<bar>:echo ""<CR>

* Press Ctrl-N to turn off highlighting.
:noremap <silent> <C-N> :silent noh<CR>
-Ashok

changed the bios to identify it as AHCI, it recognized the CD, but the dear
ol hard disks were not recognized.

But I installed  Linux, (I think FC 6 / Slackware 12 , again cannotrecall, ) with a USB CD drive, and the OS works fine. It recognises theDVD drive and the HDDs , no prob there.

I know the reply is quite unhelpful in specific, but i mean to say, if the OS is installed , it may be OK thereafter.

> Microsoft wins battle for OOXML approval
> http://news.zdnet.co.uk/software/0,1000000121,39378350,00.htm
>
>
> The International Organization for Standardization has officially
> approved Microsoft's OOXML specification as a standard.
>
> The news confirms documents leaked on Tuesday were genuine.
> Three-quarters of the "Principal Countries" involved in the vote gave
> their approval (at least two-thirds were needed) and just 14 percent of
> participating members of ISO and the International Electrotechnical
> Commission (IEC) disapproved (under a quarter was needed).
>
> According to ISO's Wednesday statement: "Subject to there being no
> formal appeals from ISO/IEC national bodies in the next two months, the
> International Standard will accordingly proceed to publication."
>
> Although there have been allegations of voting irregularities within
> some of the national standards bodies that in turn participated in the
> ISO vote, no national body has yet made a formal appeal to ISO.
>
> One prominent example had been an objection from Steve Pepper, the
> chairman of Standard Norge's joint technical committee, which he faxed
> directly to the ISO. In the letter, he claimed that 80 percent of the
> committee had been against the OOXML standard being passed ? Norway
> officially recorded a vote of approval.
>
> However, a spokesperson for Standard Norge told ZDNet.co.uk on Wednesday
> that the organisation had not made a formal appeal to ISO, and did not
> intend to do so. "One of the committee members sent a fax to ISO about
> this matter, but he did that directly and not through us," the
> spokesperson said.
>
> A spokesperson for ISO confirmed on Wednesday that it had not yet
> received any formal objections to the OOXML voting process, and refused
> to comment on the reports of voting irregularities within national
> bodies.

Qmail has something called qmailtoaster, a CentOS based ISO I think.

The better option would be to install postfix.

http://www.postfix.org

As to spam and virus filtering, there are many options.

You have a million readmes on the Internet on these matters.

clamav for virus filtering and Vipul's razor for spam control come to
mind.

But spam control involves a lot more. Like tarpitting, greylisting, RBL
checks, SPF and so on.

My del.icio might have some of them. But google is your best friend.

http://del.icio.us/girish1729

Dear Sujith,
			Alas, this is one of the problems when you go in for bleeding edge hardware 
on Linux/Other non-MS OS's. Driver development unfortunately is not as fast as 
for windows, and is often plagued by bugs in the start stages. I still 
remember the time when I had bought my nforce 430/Geforce 6150 motherboard 
(Dec 2005). Fedora Core 4, wouldnt detect the SATA controller (My hard disk 
is SATA), no audio, no LAN and even no graphics. FC5 enabled graphics (2d via 
the nv driver), SATA. Finally Nvidia released some rpms for LAN and audio and 
proper 3D drivers for the integrated graphics chipset. It was only in FC6 
(released after abt a yr, circa oct 2006), that everything worked out of the 
box (Infact everything worked from 2.6.17 kernel). So I guess with time your 
problems will stabilize. :) You can try Debian now. Maybe you can pickup the 
2.6.24.4 kernel from Sid(unstable) and see if your problems get resolved.

Regards,
Karthik Ramgopal 
BITS Pilani

From m.sujith at gmail.com  Fri Apr  4 06:48:09 2008
From: m.sujith at gmail.com (Sujith)
Date: Fri Apr  4 06:51:06 2008
Subject: [Ilugc] reg SIGSERV in pThreads
In-Reply-To: <659732.29689.qm@web8402.mail.in.yahoo.com>
References: <659732.29689.qm@web8402.mail.in.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <18421.33233.721340.147964@localhost.localdomain>

Venkatraman S writes:
 > I did notice that the RES and VIRT (obtained by 'top' cmd) kept on increasing when the program was running. 

Probably a memory leak.

 > Questions :
 > a) Fix for the above problem or atleast the hints.
 > b) How do i know the the number of threads spawned by a process in Linux - either programatically or via cmds?
 > c) How do i know the mem/resource allocated for each of the threads spawned? (read 'threads' and not 'processes')

The memory usage reported by top is highly ambiguous.
To know the exact memory usage of your application, you have to use something else.
'pmap' comes to mind. See the manpage of pmap.

Also, you can look at the contents of /proc/<pid>/smaps.
A perl tool to parse it and display in a readable format is present here:
http://www.contrib.andrew.cmu.edu/%7Ebmaurer/memory/smem.pl.
This script depends on this package: http://search.cpan.org/%7Eopi/Linux-Smaps-0.01/
Or you can run a full-fledged memory profiler. I would suggest Valgrind.

To see the threads an app has spawned, I usually use 'pstree -p'.
Threads are contained in curly braces.

And finally, gdb is very much capable of debugging threads.
See: http://sourceware.org/gdb/current/onlinedocs/gdb_5.html#SEC27

Sujith
-- 
http://m.sujith.googlepages.com
http://sujith-m.blogspot.com

On Thu, Apr 3, 2008 at 8:33 PM, Venkatraman S <blizzard_venkat@yahoo.co.in>
wrote:


> process the request. This is using pthreads. The system seems to perform
> well till it reaches the magical number of 4096 - when the 4096th request

favorites, panel or desktop as you wish.

On 15:06:00 Apr 04, K Sai Kiran wrote:
>    i see the following errors in the dmesg o/p.
> 
>    usb 1-2: new high speed USB device using ehci_hcd and address 2
>    usb 1-2: string descriptor 0 read error: -110
>    usb 1-2: configuration #1 chosen from 1 choice
>    usb 1-2: usbfs: USBDEVFS_CONTROL failed cmd f-spot rqt 128 rq 6 len 1000
>    ret -110
>    usb 1-2: usbfs: USBDEVFS_CONTROL failed cmd f-spot rqt 128 rq 6 len 1000
>    ret -110
>    usb 1-2: usbfs: USBDEVFS_CONTROL failed cmd f-spot rqt 33 rq 102 len 0 ret
>    -110
>    usb 1-2: usbfs: USBDEVFS_CONTROL failed cmd f-spot rqt 33 rq 102 len 0 ret
>    -110
>    usb 1-2: usbfs: USBDEVFS_CONTROL failed cmd f-spot rqt 33 rq 102 len 0 ret
>    -110
>    usb 1-2: reset high speed USB device using ehci_hcd and address 2
>    usb 1-2: device descriptor read/64, error -110
>    usb 1-2: device descriptor read/64, error -110
>    usb 1-2: reset high speed USB device using ehci_hcd and address 2
>    usb 1-2: USB disconnect, address 2
> 

Is this all you get in the logs?

I have only one question. Does it report as ugen0? 

If it does that then you are in trouble.

If instead it creates a storage device then you are safe.


Please send the complete log.

If this is the complete log well then your kernel doesn't support it.

ugen0 devices are unsupported. The way USB device probing works is -
there is a probing for a specific device type, then device class, if it
does not find anything it already knows then it creates a generic class
device. 

Which is another way of USB telling you "I know nothing about this."

-Girish

From rajanvn at gmail.com  Sat Apr  5 03:44:56 2008
From: rajanvn at gmail.com (Natarajan V)
Date: Sat Apr  5 03:45:16 2008
Subject: [Ilugc] Accessing Canon Powershot sx100 in Linux
In-Reply-To: <47F5F680.6070502@gmail.com>
References: <47F5F680.6070502@gmail.com>
Message-ID: <e977d4310804041514q3c70893fjfe76371f18289e15@mail.gmail.com>

On Fri, Apr 4, 2008 at 5:36 AM, K Sai Kiran <saikiranrgda@gmail.com> wrote:
>    hi,
>
>    I am trying to access a Canon Powershot SX100 IS in Fedora 8, but i am not
>    able to access it. I tried using F-spot & digi kam. Both of them are not
>    bale to connect.  I don't find the model in the supported model list. I
>    tried using Generic drivers, but no avail. I also tried using different
>    camera models from Canon, that doesn't help either.
>

Generally cameras have 2 modes of connectivity to the PC.
1. PTP mode  - Photo transfer protocol
2. Proprietary mode/ in some other cameras - USB mass storage mode

I have never owned a Cannon camera, but its worth while for you to
check, if your camera supports a PTP mode (try the USB/Connectivity
mode under the settings menu).

With PTP mode, your camera should work out of the box. If your camera
supports a USB mass storage mode, it should have been detected by now
using DigiKam/gphoto/... something similar.


HTH,

Cheers,
Natarajan.

From anoopjohn at gmail.com  Mon Apr  7 23:21:43 2008
From: anoopjohn at gmail.com (Anoop John)
Date: Mon Apr  7 23:28:47 2008
Subject: [Ilugc] GNU/Linux Install Fest in Trivandrum
Message-ID: <406f1f3f0804071051h72289882nbdac2d22629831d5@mail.gmail.com>

Dear All,

A GNU/Linux Installation fest is being arranged on 12th April, 2008 in
the heart of Trivandrum  City, by GNU/Linux Users
Group(www.ilug-tvm.org), Trivandrum and FSF India(www.fsf.org.in), in
collaboration with Zyxware Technologies(www.zyxware.com) and
SPACE(www.space-kerala.org). This fest is being organized as a part of
Dishaa '08, an event by the students of Sree Chithira Thirunal College
of Engineering, one of the pioneer engineering colleges in the city.

You can check the site of Dishaa '08 at http://www.dishaa08.com and
the page for GNU/Linux Installation Fest -
http://dishaa08.com/tech/linux/ . More details on the same can be
found in the website of GNU/Linux User Group, Trivandrum -
http://www.ilug-tvm.org/ and also in Zyxware's website -
http://www.zyxware.com/articles/2008/04/07/first-gnu-linux-install-fest-in-kerala-for-the-general-public

It is for the first time that an event of this scale, is being
organized in Trivandrum and for that matter, in Kerala. All major
press and television media have been contacted and have already
started providing coverage regarding the installation fest. We are
expecting at least 500 visitors to the stall. As part of the fest, we
will be offering Ubuntu as the primary choice
 of distro and we will distribute Ubuntu CDs to all who show interest.
Visitors will also be able to get any other GNU/Linux distro(any from
the list available at (http://www.zyxware.com/requestcd/urllist)
installed instead of Ubuntu.

We have about 12 volunteers for that day and we hope to do atleast 100
installations during the day. All those who do not bring their systems
to the fest, will get an option to register for a free installation at
a later period by Zyxware employees or ilug-tvm volunteers. A similar
program has been running successfully at Zyxware as part of our Ubuntu
Services(http://www.zyxware.com/articles/2008/01/29/get-ubuntu-installed-on-your-laptop-for-free).
Additionally we will also be providing Ubuntu bootable pen drives
during the fest(http://www.zyxware.com/articles/2008/03/26/ubuntu-live-usb-pen-drives-order-online).

We are looking forward to all the support we can get from the
community in terms of publicizing this event.

Cheers
Anoop

From ishangoel13 at gmail.com  Tue Apr  8 10:29:35 2008
From: ishangoel13 at gmail.com (ishan goel)
Date: Tue Apr  8 10:29:45 2008
Subject: [Ilugc] re: installing open solaris10 with ubuntu 7.10
In-Reply-To: <9d3184460804072141h5c9319d8v75ebdef1dc8f319a@mail.gmail.com>
References: <9d3184460804072141h5c9319d8v75ebdef1dc8f319a@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <394d59cd0804072159x6a0953fbl88e6f5119c2c80b7@mail.gmail.com>

Hi,
Even i faced a similar kind of problem but not in ubuntu but on fedora 7
when i installed solaris express edition after linux installation.What i did
was I copied the solaris grub entry

title Solaris 10 1/06
        root (hd0,2,d)
        kernel /platform/i86pc/multiboot
        module /platform/i86pc/boot_archive
the (hd0,2,d) part can vary.I copied this in /boot/grub/menu.lst and
rebooted.

Hope This works for you

ISHAN

ILUGC Meet (Apr 12th):-
=====================

Time : Sat Apr 12th 15:00 IST 2008
Venue: ADI-TeNeT Seminar Hall,
       Room No: CSD 320, 
       Electrical Science Block,
       IIT-Madras.

Map: http://chennailug.org/tenet

> Talk 1: "i-want-2-do-project. tell-me-wat-2-do"
        By Shakthi Kannan (45 mins)

Abstract:

Tutorial for newbies into Free and Open Source Software development,
and for so-called "engineering students"

Link: http://www.shakthimaan.com/downloads/glv/presentations/i-want-2-do-project-tell-me-wat-2-do.pdf


> Talk 2: SSH - Lifeline of System Admins
        By Raman P (20 mins)

Abstract:

OpenSSH, SSH connectivity tools, encrypts all traffic to effectively
eliminate eavesdropping, connection hijacking, and other attacks. It
provides secure tunneling capabilities and several authentication
methods, and supports all SSH protocol versions.

Link: http://www.openssh.org/


> Talk 3: Data Warehousing & Pentaho Open Source BI Suite
        By Ravi Jaya (30 mins)

Abstract: 

The Pentaho Open BI Suite provides a full spectrum of Business
Intelligence (BI) capabilities including reporting, analysis,
dashboards, data mining, and data integration.

Link: http://www.pentaho.com/

HTH :)

From pravi.a at gmail.com  Wed Apr  9 19:05:05 2008
From: pravi.a at gmail.com (Praveen A)
Date: Wed Apr  9 19:05:26 2008
Subject: [Ilugc] An Open Letter to Wipro, Infosys and TCS
Message-ID: <3f2beab60804090635w7253924cy4b07ecb17ba6a62a@mail.gmail.com>

http://www.fossmeet.in/node/128

6th April 2008

This letter is to express our deep disappointment over your open
support to the OOXML format forced through ISO by Microsoft. Being the
top IT giants and thus the representatives of the IT industry in the
country, it is a great shock to us that you do not stand with academia
of the country and its representatives like the IITs, IIMs and IISc in
supporting the Open Document Format (ODF) which is a true Free and
Open Standard already recognised as an ISO Standard. Considering that
a major portion of your employees come from such institutions, it is a
wonder to us that you have decided to go ahead with this decisions. We
would like to hear your explanation with respect to these points
:-(quoted from www.noooxml.org/petition)

1. There is already a standard ISO26300 named Open Document Format
(ODF): a dual standard adds costs, uncertainty and confusion to
industry, government and citizens;

2. There is no provable implementation of the OOXML specification:
Microsoft Office 2007 produces a special version of OOXML, not a file
format which complies with the OOXML specification;

3. There is information missing from the specification document, for
example how to do a ?autoSpaceLikeWord95? or
?useWord97LineBreakRules?;

4. More than 10% of the examples mentioned in the proposed standard do
not validate as XML;

5. There is no guarantee that anybody can write software that fully or
partially implements the OOXML specification without being liable to
patent lawsuits or patent license fees by Microsoft;

6. This format conflicts with existing ISO standards, such as ISO 8601
(Representation of dates and times), ISO 639 (Codes for the
Representation of Names and Languages) or ISO/IEC 10118-3
(cryptographic hash);

7. There is a bug in the spreadsheet file format which forbids any
date before the year 1900: such bugs affect the OOXML specification as
well as software applications like Microsoft Excel 2000, XP, 2003 and
2007.

8. This standard proposal was not created by bringing together the
experience and expertise of all interested parties (such as the
producers, sellers, buyers, users and regulators), but by Microsoft
alone.

With this decision, the impression you are making on your future
employees in the academia is not a very pretty one. In fact, the
development of OOXML receiving ISO?s approval has devalued our
confidence in the standards setting process itself. We hope that you
will put self-profit behind our country?s needs, change your decision,
and stand with the rest of the country on this issue.


PS:
Please forward this to the groups you are in...



--

>> of the country and its representatives like the IITs, IIMs and IISc in
>> supporting the Open Document Format (ODF) which is a true Free and
>> Open Standard already recognised as an ISO Standard. Considering that
>> a major portion of your employees come from such institutions, it is a
>> wonder to us that you have decided to go ahead with this decisions. We
>> would like to hear your explanation with respect to these points
>> :-(quoted from www.noooxml.org/petition)
>>
>> 1. There is already a standard ISO26300 named Open Document Format
>> (ODF): a dual standard adds costs, uncertainty and confusion to
>> industry, government and citizens;
>>
>> 2. There is no provable implementation of the OOXML specification:
>> Microsoft Office 2007 produces a special version of OOXML, not a file
>> format which complies with the OOXML specification;
>>
>> 3. There is information missing from the specification document, for
>> example how to do a ?autoSpaceLikeWord95? or
>> ?useWord97LineBreakRules?;
>>
>> 4. More than 10% of the examples mentioned in the proposed standard do
>> not validate as XML;
>>
>> 5. There is no guarantee that anybody can write software that fully or
>> partially implements the OOXML specification without being liable to
>> patent lawsuits or patent license fees by Microsoft;
>>
>> 6. This format conflicts with existing ISO standards, such as ISO 8601
>> (Representation of dates and times), ISO 639 (Codes for the
>> Representation of Names and Languages) or ISO/IEC 10118-3
>> (cryptographic hash);
>>
>> 7. There is a bug in the spreadsheet file format which forbids any
>> date before the year 1900: such bugs affect the OOXML specification as
>> well as software applications like Microsoft Excel 2000, XP, 2003 and
>> 2007.
>>
>> 8. This standard proposal was not created by bringing together the
>> experience and expertise of all interested parties (such as the
>> producers, sellers, buyers, users and regulators), but by Microsoft
>> alone.
>>
>> With this decision, the impression you are making on your future
>> employees in the academia is not a very pretty one. In fact, the
>> development of OOXML receiving ISO?s approval has devalued our
>> confidence in the standards setting process itself. We hope that you
>> will put self-profit behind our country?s needs, change your decision,
>> and stand with the rest of the country on this issue.
>>
>>
>> PS:
>> Please forward this to the groups you are in...
>>
>>
>>
>>
>>
>>

From prem at songbirdtech.com  Thu Apr 10 13:47:14 2008
From: prem at songbirdtech.com (Prem Kurian Philip)
Date: Thu Apr 10 13:47:22 2008
Subject: [Ilugc] Re: ilugc Digest, Vol 47, Issue 16
In-Reply-To: <20080410003013.596561DB261@www.ae.iitm.ac.in>
References: <20080410003013.596561DB261@www.ae.iitm.ac.in>
Message-ID: <50984.61.247.255.57.1207815434.squirrel@www.songbirdtech.com>

> This letter is to express our deep disappointment over your open
> support to the OOXML format forced through ISO by Microsoft. Being the
> top IT giants and thus the representatives of the IT industry in the
> country, it is a great shock to us that you do not stand with academia
> of the country and its representatives like the IITs, IIMs and IISc in
> supporting the Open Document Format (ODF) which is a true Free and
> Open Standard already recognised as an ISO Standard. Considering that
> a major portion of your employees come from such institutions, it is a
> wonder to us that you have decided to go ahead with this decisions.

None of the reasons quoted above are valid reasons for considering ODF
over OOXML. These companies cannot be expected to consider one format over
another because some of their employees come from some institute which may
prefer that format.

However, the reasons you have quoted from www.noooxml.org are all valid.

From: sudhir@openlx.com:

> You seem to be one of those great personalities that exist in all times of
> history to do the back-stabbing of the efforts of selfless people. Just
> like them, your efforts may well find you a place in history - just keep
> up with your efforts.

ISO is an organization comprised of academicians and industry. There is
nothing "selfless" about working in ISO or forming a standard. Also, this
is not about personalities.

One of the reasons for having a standard is to aid interoperability. It
just so happens that this time around OOXML was adopted as a standard -
and this is not the first time an inferior format has been adopted as the
standard by the ISO.

From: sudhir@openlx.com:
> The trouble, that goes in favour of people like you and companies like the
> m$ and these 4 big ones is : No one cares for the country, no one cares
> for the world - all are bothered about their pockets alone. And, in that
> priority,  everything like the society, the good of the world, the
> country, the family - just everything other than the bank-balance, are
> lost. So is the case of most of the peple at these institutions who start
> counting their bank balance even before completing theier studies.In such
> circumstances, whet is the worth of selfless acts of a few who care for
> the world ?

You are implying that these companies got paid off by MS for supporting
OOXML. That is a serious allegation to make without any evidence. Also, I
don't think there is anything selfless about forming a standard.

Also, I think we are making too much about these standards in anycase and
particularly so in the Indian context.

How does the standardization by ISO affect us in any case? Can the
government mandate that all organizations shift to using MS software? and
even if they did, will all organizations comply?

I could be wrong, but I don't think it will make much of a difference.

Regards,
PK

I dont know if there is any such direct converter available
But my solution will be to exploit IDL of CORBA

Steps are
1. C -> IDL
2. IDL -> Java

idlj compiler is an  IDL-to-Java Compiler which is part of SUN Java SDK
GCC does not have IDL support presently.
I dont know what is the software for converting C to IDL
We have to find an ORB which comes with a C to IDL conversion facility.

IMO C to Java conversion using software is bad.

On Mon, Mar 31, 2008 at 11:40 AM, Dharma lingam <rdharmalingam@gmail.com> wrote:
> Pls switch to root account
>  $ sudo su -

To set root password, use

$ sudo passwd root

This will fist ask you for the logged in user's password. Later you
are prompted to enter and confirm the root user's password. But as
mentioned earlier, use "sudo" rather than logging in as root.

From prem at songbirdtech.com  Fri Apr 11 11:46:51 2008
From: prem at songbirdtech.com (Prem Kurian Philip)
Date: Fri Apr 11 11:47:03 2008
Subject: [Ilugc] re: Open Source code convertor, from C to Java
Message-ID: <50051.61.247.255.57.1207894611.squirrel@www.songbirdtech.com>

> I dont know if there is any such direct converter available
> But my solution will be to exploit IDL of CORBA
>
> Steps are
> 1. C -> IDL
> 2. IDL -> Java
>
> idlj compiler is an  IDL-to-Java Compiler which is part of SUN Java SDK
> GCC does not have IDL support presently.
> I dont know what is the software for converting C to IDL
> We have to find an ORB which comes with a C to IDL conversion facility.

This won't work. IDL-to-Java compiler is used for generating C++ code from
IDL descriptors. IDL is a language independent way of describing
interfaces exposed by a CORBA server.

If you want to know something about CORBA and IDL, please see:
http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Interface_description_language

Read up a little about RMI - that will give you some idea.

For converting C code to Java, you will most likely need to do it by hand.

Thanks,
PK

From prem at songbirdtech.com  Fri Apr 11 11:48:07 2008
From: prem at songbirdtech.com (Prem Kurian Philip)
Date: Fri Apr 11 11:48:15 2008
Subject: [Ilugc] re: Open Source code convertor, from C to Java
Message-ID: <50056.61.247.255.57.1207894687.squirrel@www.songbirdtech.com>

Correction:

IDL-to-Java compiler is used for generating *Java* code and not C++ code
from IDL descriptors.

Regards,
PK

From udinesh5 at gmail.com  Fri Apr 11 13:56:56 2008
From: udinesh5 at gmail.com (Dinesh Uthayakumar)
Date: Fri Apr 11 13:57:06 2008
Subject: [Ilugc] re: Open Source code convertor, from C to Java
In-Reply-To: <50051.61.247.255.57.1207894611.squirrel@www.songbirdtech.com>
References: <50051.61.247.255.57.1207894611.squirrel@www.songbirdtech.com>
Message-ID: <683a0f200804110126p3e5bbf6bge475c8179a9a993b@mail.gmail.com>

On Fri, Apr 11, 2008 at 11:46 AM, Prem Kurian Philip <prem@songbirdtech.com>
wrote:

> IDL is a language independent way of describing
> interfaces exposed by a CORBA server.


I dint mean the procedure will lead to a complete Java code.
I do know that CORBA is used for distributed computing, making different
software components on possibly different platform to communicate to each
other

For converting C code to Java, you will most likely need to do it by hand.
>

let me be more specific.
C language to IDL conversion will generate IDL module with interfaces.
idlj will create Interface and Implementation skeleton classes.
now we have to implement the interfaces in appropriate classes.
here i am not using the CORBA packages nor registering any references, but
just exploiting the IDL feature.

hope i am clear :)

Hey Zico,

On Sat, Mar 29, 2008 at 1:14 AM, Zico <mailzico@gmail.com> wrote:
> I am using shared broadband connection in my Debian laptop at home. I am
>  having an annoying problem regarding my internet connection. My problem is:
>  after some times my connection is gone automatically. Sometimes it occurs
>  after 10 minutes & sometimes it occurs after 1/2 hours. Here, "connection
>  gone" means..."Destination Host unreachable". But, if i reboot my laptop, it
>  becomes ok again & same problem happens after some time. Reboot... ok...
>  again gone...reboot...ok... so on.

Are you sure this problem is related to your laptop? You Internet
connection might be to blame as well. Line noise will sever the
connection and the DSL router will try to reconnect on its own. In the
time that you are rebooting you laptop, it might be reconnecting back.
Watch the LEDs on the modem and make sure the LED representing the
remote side of the connection is behaving as expected.

Hi All,

I have a few PC Engines WRAP x86 boards for sale.  The
hardware is the size of a CDROM, and runs a variety of
unmodified Linux 386 distros (no cross-compilation
necessary).  Ideally suited for Linux based embedded
network servers, data loggers, and other special
applications.

The devices have no moving parts or fans, are exceptionally
reliable and consume 3-5W of power.  These boards are
completely unused and still in their original packaging.

The boards include:
  * 233Mhz AMD Geode SC1100 x86 CPU
  * 128MB RAM
  * Storage using CF card (supports any CF card upto 2GB)
  * 100BT NIC (with Power over Ethernet support)
  * RS232 serial port
  * NO video support, the boards are headless

  * 12-18V DC power supply and CF card not included
     You can get these at your fav Ritchie St. vendor.

More hardware details here:
    http://www.pcengines.ch/wrap.htm

Please contact me *off list* in case you are interested.

I can make special allowances for anyone who will use
this hardware to develop open source applications.

Thanks!

- Raja

Subject: [Ilugc] Bangalore,
	15th April: Candle light vigil for Document Freedom
Message-ID: <3f2beab60804132116t6e80cad0wd9ff68647756d094@mail.gmail.com>

Dear Friends,

Recently International Standardisation Organisation (ISO) is approved
Microsoft's broken standard OOXML( with 1000s of Technical Flaws) also
as a Document standard. India's Vote was No to this standard that
creates vendor lock-in and prevents interoperability. Micro$oft played
a lot of nasty games to get the approval from member countries. In this
context we are Conducting a Candle Light Vigil for Document Freedom
Demanding bureau of indian standard (BIS) to appeal ISO's Decision of
approving the banana standard OOXML

Venue : In Front of Townhall, Corporation Circle , Bangalore
Date : 15th April 6.00pm

The programme is planned as a starting point for
various events & awareness campaigns on  Document freedom .

Please use   following wiki page for organising the programme
http://fci.wikia.com/wiki/Campaign_for_Document_Freedom

Also add your name on campaigners section

Contact : Praveen A <pravi.a at gmail.com> +91 9986348565
Anivar Aravind <anivar at movingrepublic dot org> +91 9449009908/ +91
080 23435606


Why Document Freedom?

We live in an age in which paper documents increasingly get replaced
by electronic records. Document freedom is fundamental for your
documents to outlive the application you are currently using and
allows you to choose and change applications freely.

Previous proprietary document formats have become difficult or
impossible to read within little more than a decade. There is no
reason to believe this trend will not continue if allowed so to do.
Without open standards for our documents we are likely to inflict a
'digital dark-age' on our descendants when they discover that they are
unable to read any of the sources for their history, such as
Government records, acts of Parliament, property title deeds,
scientific research papers, and family histories. They will not
forgive us if we fail to act to protect them now, but instead allow
another generation of poorly specified proprietary standards to become
widely adopted.

Document Freedom and Democracy

Electronic records kept today include records of your government, such
as tax and legal records or minutes of parliamentary proceedings.
Making sure that such records remain in the control of the government
is essential for a functioning democracy. The same is true for all
interactions between citizens and their government, which should never
depend on monopolies or on the proprietary product of a single company.

How to achieve Document Freedom?

Make a stand by saving your documents in ODF today. If your application
does not support ODF, get one of the ODF supported applications like
OpenOffice.org, Staroffice, NeoOffice, KOffice, AbiWord, Google Docs,
IBM Lotus Symphony etc

We request all users to

  1. not send attachments in proprietary formats like .doc, .xls, .ppt
  2. not pollute their friends computers and the internet with
unethically encoded documents.
  3. inform the users that they do not have right to decode the
documents they themselves have written, if they use proprietary
software
  4. distribute open office cds, containing apps with source code for windows.
  5. distribute live cds.

Regards
Praveen

From sbharathi at MidasComm.Com  Mon Apr 14 19:05:37 2008
From: sbharathi at MidasComm.Com (Bharathi Subramanian)
Date: Mon Apr 14 19:02:52 2008
Subject: [Ilugc] One Day One GNU/Linux Command (MAN)
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0804141248490.1385-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>

One Day One GNU/Linux Command
=============================

man - Format and display the 'MAN'ual pages.

Summary: 

Most of the commands are comes with a specially formatted manual,
which explains "how to use the command, option list, etc..".
'man' command is used to view those manual page.

Man pages are sorted in categories, as mentioned below:

1. Executable programs / Shell commands
2. System calls
3. Library calls 
4. Special files
5. Config file formats and conventions 
6. Games
7. Miscellaneous
8. System administration commands
9. Non-standard

Examples:

$ man man -- Display the manual page of the man command

$ man ls -- Display the manual page of the ls command

$ man printf -- Display printf command man page.

$ man 3 printf -- Display printf lib call man page.

$ man resolv.conf -- Display the manual page of DNS Config file.

$ man ./myman -- Display the myman page present in the local dir.

Man page location: /usr/share/man/manX

For more info, Read: man man

Bye :)
--
Bharathi S

From pravi.a at gmail.com  Tue Apr 15 09:00:52 2008
From: pravi.a at gmail.com (Praveen A)
Date: Tue Apr 15 09:01:04 2008
Subject: [Ilugc] The Hindu: Techies protest proprietary standards;
	seek policy
Message-ID: <3f2beab60804142030o40e29946o3099080e04f1625b@mail.gmail.com>

Today's Hindu has a report on Candle Light Vigil and Campaign for
Document Freedom.

BANGALORE: Ever since the International Standardisation Organisation
(ISO) vote on April 2 adopted Microsoft's Office Open XML (OOXML) as a
document standard, techie blogs and websites have been inundated with
posts and articles voicing their opposition to proprietary software
and technical issues with the new standard.

Organisations and online communities ? such as the Free Software User
Group and the Free and Open Source Software ? are looking to raise the
issue more aggressively in the public domain. "We call the OOXML
format a "banana standard." Besides raising awareness, we want the
Government to formulate a policy supporting Open Software and also
appeal the ISO mandate," said Anivar Aravind, a software consultant
who will participate in a rally in front of the Town Hall on Tuesday
to raise awareness about Open Document formats and demand a national
policy on standardisation and use of Open Software.

In simple words, the problem is one of compatibility, an important
issue in this digital world. For example, take the much hyped
e-governance. If the Government maintains its land records in a
certain digital format, and the documentation uses a proprietary
format, then a user will have to keep upgrading his operating system
to access the record. Proponents of Free Software argue that even with
Microsoft's old document format (.doc), a file created seven to eight
years ago may not be recognised by a modern operating systems such as
XP. "This is like being sold a house without being given the key to
it. We need public support to take it to the policy level," says
Venkatesh Hariharan, who was part of a Bureau of Indian Standards
(BIS) committee.

The BIS, which represents India at ISO, had 19 members of which 13
voted against Microsoft's OOXML. Many academics and colleges
(NIT-Calicut among others) have written open letters to TCS, Infosys,
NASSCOM, Wipro (that voted to abstain) and Microsoft (voted in favour
of OOXML). There is a rising fear among academics and advocates of
free software standards that BIS will come under pressure in the
absence of any national policy. Tamil Nadu and Kerala are the only two
States who have a policy in place.

"Very big voices like NASSCOM and Infosys that have not participated
in even one meeting have voted irresponsibly. We fear that if such
lobbying continues, academics and individuals like us will be put on
the defensive, unless there is a policy in place," said Nagarjuna G.,
professor at the Tata Institute of Fundamental Research, who was part
of the technical committee of BIS. This committee alone identified
200-odd technical flaws in OOXML's 7,000 page document ? the Open
Document Format is 600 pages ? and more than 1,000 others were
identified internationally.

The National Knowledge Commission Report 2006 and the Eleventh Five
Year plan for Information Technology recommend Free Software.

http://www.hindu.com/2008/04/15/stories/2008041554380500.htm

From sbharathi at MidasComm.Com  Tue Apr 15 09:59:14 2008
From: sbharathi at MidasComm.Com (Bharathi Subramanian)
Date: Tue Apr 15 09:55:56 2008
Subject: [Ilugc] One Day One GNU/Linux Command (WHATIS)
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0804150945010.2040-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>

One Day One GNU/Linux Command 
=============================

whatis -- Search the whatis database for complete words.

Summary:

Whatis DB contains the name and one line description about 
all man pages.  whatis searches for keywords and  displays 
the result(s).  Only complete  word matches are displayed.

Examples:

$ whatis ls -- Show small info about ls command.

$ whatis perl -- Show small info about Perl.

$ whatis gcc -- Show small info about GCC command.

$ whatis printf -- Show small info about printf.

$ whatis socket -- Show small info about socket.

$ whatis compile -- Just try (Error).

Location of whatis DB: /var/cache/man/whatis

Read: man whatis

HTH :)
--
Bharathi S

From lawgon at thenilgiris.com  Tue Apr 15 13:37:31 2008
From: lawgon at thenilgiris.com (Kenneth Gonsalves)

Subject: [Ilugc] [commercial] Set up and maintain systems
Message-ID: <DD178BAD-AFBE-4327-A337-8534E91CD897@thenilgiris.com>

Hi,

AU-KBC Centre at MIT requires a concern experienced in setting up and  
maintaining LANs to configure it's network and maintain the same. The  
network comprises 175 machines, mixed Linux and windows. There are  
three ISPs for internet connection, firewall server, dhcp server,  
file server, mail server and dns server. These are to be configured  
to route the internet connection with load balancing and failover.  
There are several servers that are running web services on the LAN  
and these are to be forwarded to the internet for external access.  
VPN has also to be set up.

Once configured and set up, there is in house support for day to day  
running of the network under external supervision, but the concern  
would have to give support for one year at the initial period.  
Needless to say, all servers would run linux and free software.

We will pay commercial rates for this. Interested persons may contact  
me offlist.

man -k net

will print all commands which contains 'net' in their name.

Bharathi Subramanian wrote:
| One Day One GNU/Linux Command
| =============================
|
| man - Format and display the 'MAN'ual pages.
|
| Summary:
|
| Most of the commands are comes with a specially formatted manual,
| which explains "how to use the command, option list, etc..".
| 'man' command is used to view those manual page.
|
| Man pages are sorted in categories, as mentioned below:
|
| 1. Executable programs / Shell commands
| 2. System calls
| 3. Library calls
| 4. Special files
| 5. Config file formats and conventions
| 6. Games
| 7. Miscellaneous
| 8. System administration commands
| 9. Non-standard
|
| Examples:
|
| $ man man -- Display the manual page of the man command
|
| $ man ls -- Display the manual page of the ls command
|
| $ man printf -- Display printf command man page.
|
| $ man 3 printf -- Display printf lib call man page.
|
| $ man resolv.conf -- Display the manual page of DNS Config file.
|
| $ man ./myman -- Display the myman page present in the local dir.
|
| Man page location: /usr/share/man/manX
|
| For more info, Read: man man
|
| Bye :)
| --
| Bharathi S
|
| _______________________________________________
| To unsubscribe, email ilugc-request@ae.iitm.ac.in with
| "unsubscribe <password> <address>"
| in the subject or body of the message.
| http://www.ae.iitm.ac.in/mailman/listinfo/ilug

From prem at songbirdtech.com  Wed Apr 16 10:57:44 2008
From: prem at songbirdtech.com (Prem Kurian Philip)
Date: Wed Apr 16 10:57:59 2008
Subject: [Ilugc] Re: The Hindu: Techies protest proprietary standards;
	seek policy
In-Reply-To: <20080416042053.291221DB273@www.ae.iitm.ac.in>
References: <20080416042053.291221DB273@www.ae.iitm.ac.in>
Message-ID: <49272.61.247.255.57.1208323664.squirrel@www.songbirdtech.com>

>>  Another classic example of some journalist who knows a little bit about
>>  the issue but not enough to write intelligently on the subject.
>
> Another classical Indian. Thanks. How about coming up with something
> that common people can understand?
>
> We are at least lighting a candle, think what you are doing?

You are perhaps motivated to do these things. I am not. But I do know
enough about these formats and the discussions behind it to give some
input. I don't think my input is valid only if I hold a candle.

I see a lot of discussions about the OOXML vs ODF in India and most of it
is pretty misinformed.

>>
>>  Also, the .DOC format is different from the OOXML format.
>
> Both are proprietary formats controlled by Microosft, now the latter
> got blessed by ISO, that is the problem here.
>
> Only Microsoft can implement doc format perfectly since only they have
> the specs. Similar is the case with OOXML - but even though you have a
> spec out there, that is insufficient and you need to pay up Microsoft.

This is not true. One of the conditions for a format to be standardized is
that it should conform to the Open Specification Promise (OSP) which
allows for products to use this format without any patent disputes arising
from it and without the payment of royalties to MS.

I suggest that you verify this for yourself by looking at the information
about OOXML on the web.

Regards,
PK

From sbharathi at MidasComm.Com  Wed Apr 16 11:45:07 2008
From: sbharathi at MidasComm.Com (Bharathi Subramanian)
Date: Wed Apr 16 11:41:43 2008
Subject: [Ilugc] One Day One GNU/Linux Command (INFO)
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0804161128520.3695-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>

One Day One GNU/Linux Command
=============================

info - Display documentation in Info format.

Summary: 

Apart from Man pages, some commands comes with a detail manual pages,
called info pages, which is in info format. This info command provides
Menu, Search, Corss-Ref and many other facilities. Press ? to get
on-line info help.

Examples:

$ info  -- List all info pages available in the system.

$ info emacs -- Show Emacs info page. (See man emacs, to feel the 
                 difference)

$ info --show-options gcc -- Show the GCC command line options

$ pinfo libc -- Curses based lynx-style info browser.

Info files location: /usr/share/info/

Read: info info, info pinfo

HTH :)
-- 
Bharathi S

>> about  the issue but not enough to write intelligently on the
subject.
>
> Another classical Indian. Thanks. How about coming up with something 
> that common people can understand?
>
> We are at least lighting a candle, think what you are doing?

You are perhaps motivated to do these things. I am not. But I do know
enough about these formats and the discussions behind it to give some
input. I don't think my input is valid only if I hold a candle.

I see a lot of discussions about the OOXML vs ODF in India and most of
it is pretty misinformed.

>>
>>  Also, the .DOC format is different from the OOXML format.
>
> Both are proprietary formats controlled by Microosft, now the latter 
> got blessed by ISO, that is the problem here.
>
> Only Microsoft can implement doc format perfectly since only they have

> the specs. Similar is the case with OOXML - but even though you have a

> spec out there, that is insufficient and you need to pay up Microsoft.

This is not true. One of the conditions for a format to be standardized
is that it should conform to the Open Specification Promise (OSP) which
allows for products to use this format without any patent disputes
arising from it and without the payment of royalties to MS.

I suggest that you verify this for yourself by looking at the
information about OOXML on the web.

Kg,

From: Kenneth Gonsalves <lawgon@thenilgiris.com>
>> This is not true. One of the conditions for a format to be
>> standardized is
>> that it should conform to the Open Specification Promise (OSP) which
>> allows for products to use this format without any patent disputes
>> arising
>> from it and without the payment of royalties to MS.
>
> M$ have promised not to sue. But there are two problems here. One is
> that they havent given the list of patents (assuming they have a
> list) and secondly a promise not backed by consideration is not
> enforceable in law. In other words, there is nothing to prevent them
> from breaking their promise and suing

The difference is that the OSP is effectively a sublicensing of MS patents.

While it is a one-sided Patent promise and while it is true that a promise
without a backing consideration is not enforceable under law, it is
interesting to note that the OpenDocument Format (ODF) is also a one-sided
patent promise from Sun on the same terms:
http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Open_Specification_Promise

Perhaps I am missing something - I am not a lawyer and since you are,
perhaps you can throw some light on this subject as the licensing terms
from Sun (for OpenDocument) and from MS (for OOXML) seem pretty similar?

Regards,
PK

From prem at songbirdtech.com  Wed Apr 16 14:27:13 2008
From: prem at songbirdtech.com (Prem Kurian Philip)
Date: Wed Apr 16 14:27:46 2008
Subject: [Ilugc] Re: The Hindu: Techies protest 
	proprietarystandards; seek policy
In-Reply-To: <20080416082415.F32121DB271@www.ae.iitm.ac.in>
References: <20080416082415.F32121DB271@www.ae.iitm.ac.in>
Message-ID: <50860.61.247.255.57.1208336233.squirrel@www.songbirdtech.com>

From: "Senthil Sundaram (sensunda)" <sensunda@cisco.com>

> Hi Prem,
>
> If u are in blr and would like to talk on ooxml ... And maybe someone
> from fsug can
> Talk on why no ooxml..lets get the debate to the open..as part of the
> campaign for document freedom.

I am actually in Chennai. I may not be able to come to Bangalore to speak
on the subject. However, I can post information about OOXML (pros and
cons) on ilugc.

About my own stand on the topic - I believe ODF is a better format and
should have been selected by ISO instead of OOXML. However, the reasons
quoted against OOXML being selected aren't always based on fact. My desire
is to point out these problems.

There are many good reasons why OOXML is an inferior format and shouldn't
have been selected. It is important for those campaigning against OOXML to
get these facts right about both ODF and OOXML and fight OOXML on the
facts rather than being led by emotion or by an irrational/rational hatred
of MS which is common among Linux users.

I think it is also pertinent to look at how this affects India - because
the way things work here in India is quite different from how things get
done in the EU, US etc.

Regards,
PK

> Menu, Search, Corss-Ref and many other facilities. Press ? to get
> on-line info help.

Why are there two different formats: Because Man was developed for BSD at
UC Berkeley, whereas Info was developed for GNU at MIT.

Also: I recommend running info from within Emacs: "emacs -f info", mainly
because it colorizes the headings.

1. Is there any way to colorize the headings without Emacs?

2. How can I tell Emacs to show the Emacs Info page, from the command line?
   "emacs -f 'info emacs'" does not work :-(

-- 
Masatran, R. Deepak <http://research.iiit.ac.in/~masatran/>

From prem at songbirdtech.com  Wed Apr 16 23:01:15 2008
From: prem at songbirdtech.com (Prem Kurian Philip)
Date: Wed Apr 16 23:01:30 2008
Subject: [Ilugc] ODF vs OOXML
Message-ID: <1231.122.164.228.30.1208367075.squirrel@www.songbirdtech.com>

From: Rahul Sundaram <sundaram@fedoraproject.org>

>Umm. ODF has already been a ISO standard for a few years now.

yes, I realize that. But though ISO can set standards and ODF is a
standard, whether a format is accepted as a standard in reality by users
(that is, whether it is adopted widely) is dependent on if there is enough
ground swell of support for the format from actual users.

The implication of OOXML standardisation is that it could force
organizations (especially in the US and EU member states) to use OOXML as
a format when dealing with government projects and this will force down
the usage of ODF.

When ISO accepted OOXML as a standard, they did, in a sense, dilute ODF's
chance of becoming a "real" standard. Which is why, if you have noticed
the discussions on the topic, you will notice that the current debate
about the ISO standardization of OOXML is projected primarily as a OOXML
vs ODF competition.

Regards,
PK

> standard, whether a format is accepted as a standard in reality by users

Standardization is not just dependent on grass root support. It depends 
on what Governments choose and that is what people dealing with standard 
bodies are focused on. Too early to speculate on the impact of ISO 
approving two competing specifications but keep a eye on

http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OpenDocument_adoption

2008/4/16 Prem Kurian Philip <prem@songbirdtech.com>:
> The difference is that the OSP is effectively a sublicensing of MS patents.
>
> While it is a one-sided Patent promise and while it is true that a promise
> without a backing consideration is not enforceable under law, it is
> interesting to note that the OpenDocument Format (ODF) is also a one-sided
> patent promise from Sun on the same terms:
> http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Open_Specification_Promise
>
> Perhaps I am missing something - I am not a lawyer and since you are,
> perhaps you can throw some light on this subject as the licensing terms
> from Sun (for OpenDocument) and from MS (for OOXML) seem pretty similar?

See the analysis done by lawyers at Software Freedom Law Center
http://www.softwarefreedom.org/resources/2008/osp-gpl.pdf

They are the authoritative legal opinion of the Free Software
community and they have concluded that you can't rely on osp for a
free software implementation.

Also see their analysis of odf's patent promise to see the difference

Message-ID: <987DC348-673E-481D-9BC9-BF065C4D2C2E@thenilgiris.com>


On 17-Apr-08, at 5:18 AM, Praveen A wrote:

> This campaign is about educating users about the importance of
> document freedom and lighting candle is simbolic and only the
> beginning. There is a lot to do and we need all the help possible. It
> is a community campaign and every bit counts.

as far as I am concerned, the question is simply: which is better? I  
am not in the business of writing office applications, but am in the  
business of writing web pages - to write a web page, there are two  
phases:
1. write it according to standards
2. break the standards so that IE can read it
3. work around the breaks so that standards compliant browsers can  
read it.

simple

but it would be simpler if steps 2 and 3 could be avoided. But then  
web design might become easy, and people will stop paying web  
designers. Look at this:


Format	Text Color	Text Alignment
OOXML Text	<w:color w:val="FF0000"/>	<w:jc w:val="right"/>
OOXML Sheet	<color rgb="FFFF0000"/>	<alignment horizontal="right"/>
OOXML Presentation	<a:srgbClr val="FF0000"/>	<a:pPr algn="r"/>
ODF Text	<style:text-properties fo:color="#FF0000"/>	<style:paragraph- 
properties fo:text-align="end" />
ODF Sheet	<style:text-properties fo:color="#FF0000"/>	 
<style:paragraph-properties fo:text-align="end"/>
ODF Presentation	<style:text-properties fo:color="#FF0000"/>	 
<style:paragraph-properties fo:text-align="end"/>

as you can see, M$ uses three different syntaxes for text alignment:  
'w:jc', 'alignment' and 'algn' whereas ODF just uses 'align'.  
Similarly with colour. So, as a designer I would definetly go for  
OOXML, because only a real expert can use it, so I get paid more.  
This analysis is taken from here:
http://www.robweir.com/blog/2008/03/disharmony-of-ooxml.html

or take dates: for the last 400 years or so it has been a standard  
that 1900 is not a leap year. Until 00XML came around and created  
1900-2-29 - a non-existent date that needs to be 'pretended' to exist  
for date arithmetic to work. Details here:

http://www.robweir.com/blog/2006/10/leap-back.html

again, as a coder, I would prefer OOXML - more work for me, more pay.

-- 

regards
kg
http://lawgon.livejournal.com

From sbharathi at MidasComm.Com  Thu Apr 17 10:49:53 2008
From: sbharathi at MidasComm.Com (Bharathi Subramanian)
Date: Thu Apr 17 10:46:43 2008
Subject: [Ilugc] One Day One GNU/Linux Command (LS)
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0804171031450.4971-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>

One Day One GNU/Linux Command
=============================

ls -- List directory contents

Summary : 

List the current directory contents and informations.

Examples :

$ ls  -- Alphabetically list all files and Dir 

$ ls --color=always -- Output in color

$ ls -F -- Files are classified with /@|= symbols

$ ls -1 -- Output in single column

$ ls -a -- Display hidden entries starting with .

$ ls -R -- Recursive output

$ ls -Q -- Enclose entry names in double quotes

$ ls -lh -- List file is long format and show size in 
            human readable form like KB, MB, GB, ..

$ ls -m -- List file in comma separated entries.

$ ls -lt -- Sort and show by last modification time.

$ ls -lu -- Sort and show by last access time.

$ ls -rlu -- Show in reverse order.

Read : man ls

HTH :)
-- 
Bharathi S

From prem at songbirdtech.com  Thu Apr 17 10:55:07 2008
From: prem at songbirdtech.com (Prem Kurian Philip)
Date: Thu Apr 17 10:55:28 2008
Subject: [Ilugc] Re: The Hindu: Techies protest proprietary standards;
	seek policy
Message-ID: <49265.61.247.255.57.1208409907.squirrel@www.songbirdtech.com>

From: Kenneth Gonsalves <lawgon@thenilgiris.com>

> Similarly with colour. So, as a designer I would definetly go for
> OOXML, because only a real expert can use it, so I get paid more.
> This analysis is taken from here:
> http://www.robweir.com/blog/2008/03/disharmony-of-ooxml.html


> again, as a coder, I would prefer OOXML - more work for me, more pay.

I understand what you are getting at, but the intent in creating a
document standard is not to make it possible for people to create these
documents using just a text editor.

The intent of a standard is interoperability; that is, it should be
possible for software vendors to develop products which can be used to
view, create or modify documents which conform exactly to the
specification that has been standardized.

This is true for other formats as well: Postscript, PDF, SVG or any number
of image formats.. it is very difficult though possible to create
documents conforming to these standards using a simple text editor instead
of a specialized tool, however, that is not the recommended way to
generate these documents.

What makes OOXML more problematic is that some embedded content can be in
patent encumbered formats such as VML etc.

Also, the standard should ensure tool independence - that is, a document
generated using one tool should be 100% usable in another tool which
understands that specification. Here there are issues with OOXML because
of some undefined tags which only MS Office will truly understand or use.

There is this additional problem of binary blobs which are more difficult
to solve. This also makes it difficult to convert documents generated in
legacy formats like .DOC for usage on platforms other than MS Windows. I
will cover this in another email.

Regards,
PK

>>> They are the authoritative legal opinion of the Free Software

>> approval of usage of samba/file sharing protocol related documentation

>> that.
> They are the authoritative legal opinion of the Free Software
> community and they have concluded that you can't rely on osp for a
> free software implementation.
>

To tell you the truth, I am quite confused about this stuff because there
are completely contrary legal opinions on this subject. I quote wikipedia
below: (Please see the quote from a lawyer from the Software Freedom Law
Centre who seems to give a completely different take on the subject from
the link that you sent me)

http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Office_Open_XML

<---- Start quote ---->

Several standards and OSS licensing experts expressed support in 2006 of
the OSP. A 2006 article in Cover Pages quotes Lawrence Rosen, an attorney
and lecturer at Stanford Law School, as saying,

"I'm pleased that this OSP is compatible with free and open source licenses."

In 2006, Mark Webbink; a lawyer and member of the board of the Software
Freedom Law Center, and former employee of Linux vendor Red Hat; has said,

"Red Hat believes that the text of the OSP gives sufficient flexibility to
implement the listed specifications in software licensed under free and
open source licenses. We commend Microsoft?s efforts to reach out to
representatives from the open source community and solicit their feedback
on this text, and Microsoft's willingness to make modifications in
response to our comments."

Standards lawyer Andy Updegrove said in 2006 the Open Specification
Promise was

"what I consider to be a highly desirable tool for facilitating the
implementation of open standards, in particular where those standards are
of interest to the open source community."

<---- End quote ---->

So as you can see, the subject is not nearly as clearly defined as either
side of the debate would like us to believe.

Regards,
PK

From sbharathi at MidasComm.Com  Fri Apr 18 10:25:47 2008
From: sbharathi at MidasComm.Com (Bharathi Subramanian)
Date: Fri Apr 18 10:27:45 2008
Subject: [Ilugc] One Day One GNU/Linux Command (ECHO)
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0804181014020.6995-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>

One Day One GNU/Linux Command
=============================

echo - Display a line of text on the screen

Summary: 

Echo is used to show a line of text on the screen with limited Esc
sequence (BELL, Backspace, H-Tab, V-Tab,...) handling capabilities.

Example:

$ echo  -- Display a empty line

$ echo $HOME -- Display the env variable value.

$ echo -n "No new line" -- Display with-out trailing newline.

$ echo "Bharathi\nILUGC" -- Display the line, as it is.

$ echo -e "Bharathi\n\tILUGC" -- Interpret and show the line

$ echo -e "\033[1;34m ILUGC \033[0m" -- Display with color.

Read: man echo

HTH :)
--
Bharathi S

>  looks like Guido van Rossum prefers Django (
>  http://www.artima.com/weblogs/viewpost.jsp?thread=158931 ).

Use the framework whose programming language you are comfortable with.
If you are comfortable with Ruby use Rails with Python use either of the two.
Knowing the programming language well can help utilize the full functionaility
of the framework. Don't just use any framework because some one prefers it. Use
the one that you are comfortable with.
Fedora uses TG for all their webapps.
Tabblo, Curse Gaming, Washington Post use Django and are very large apps.

>  # Am trying to build an app which will have millions of concurrent users and
>  is going to be highly distributed.
>  # It should scale really well and does not go astray when in use.
>  # I am comfortable with pragramming, but do not want to essentially take
>  care of low level programming(and hence i like Python's way).
>  # Cleaner integration with Ajax libs would be also required.
>  # Easy on the database (will be using a replicated/clustered MySQL), hence
>  an easy to use ORM

If you are planning to go for concurrent users and require transaction
support then
none of the three will fit your bill. And MySQL will not help your situation.
My 2 cents, if a framework bundles a JS Library along with it, I consider it a
deficiency because the user will not have the freedom of choice.

>  Any 'sincere' advice or hints would be great :)

>From my experience of having used Django, I have found it really good.
The documentation
is excellent, the community is helpful and the developers believe in
perfection and
conceptual integrity.

I can't comment on the rest two because I have not used them.

The choice is yours, make use of it judiciously and not on loose talk.

--

Thejaswi Puthraya
http://thejaswi.info/

From joe_steeve at gmx.net  Fri Apr 18 14:37:43 2008
From: joe_steeve at gmx.net (Joe Steeve)
Date: Fri Apr 18 14:38:00 2008
Subject: [Ilugc] Limit on Sub-folders / Files in Linux
In-Reply-To: <fad10ddf0804161606t546e530bs8f05be7ab63ec7f@mail.gmail.com>
	(Sundar's message of "Wed\, 16 Apr 2008 18\:06\:48 -0500")
References: <863aq72q2w.fsf@lark.home>
	<Pine.LNX.4.44.0803311549490.2299-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>
	<fad10ddf0804161606t546e530bs8f05be7ab63ec7f@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <86r6d3a5uo.fsf@lark.home>

Sundar <cybertoast@gmail.com> writes:

> I'm curious about why this limit still exists in the 2.6 kernel
> - it seems like this is a throwback to some older space-saving
> mechanism, at least at first glance. AFAICT all other modern
> OS's have

> I'm going to also hit this limit soon with a media server I'm
> administering, and I'm wondering if there are ways around this
> that people have actually tried (anything from resetting the
> limit in the kernel and recompiling, to hacks in the
> procfs). Any ideas?

Even if you manage to fix the issue today by increasing the limit,
you still will come back to the same point when you hit the
new-limit.

You'll have to fix the application and make it split them up into
multiple sub-folders.

If you have 32k entries in a single directory, each 'open file'
would have to iterate through 32k entries. If your media-server is
serving a large base, this could be a problem because the
media-server application has to open these media files quite
frequently.

--

through InnoDB but it still lags behind in features like Stored Procs,
sub-queries, triggers etc.

From cybertoast at gmail.com  Fri Apr 18 22:26:51 2008
From: cybertoast at gmail.com (Sundar)
Date: Fri Apr 18 22:27:12 2008
Subject: [Ilugc] Limit on Sub-folders / Files in Linux
In-Reply-To: <86r6d3a5uo.fsf@lark.home>
References: <863aq72q2w.fsf@lark.home>
	<Pine.LNX.4.44.0803311549490.2299-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>
	<fad10ddf0804161606t546e530bs8f05be7ab63ec7f@mail.gmail.com>
	<86r6d3a5uo.fsf@lark.home>
Message-ID: <fad10ddf0804180956o241be961s2223a2f6e0382822@mail.gmail.com>

>
>
> Even if you manage to fix the issue today by increasing the limit,
> you still will come back to the same point when you hit the
> new-limit.


Which is why I'm curious about the reason for the 32k limit - why is this a
hard-coded limit? If it's a type limit (say int16) then it should be a power
of 2, not a nice round number. And if it can be increased, why is it set to
a lower number (a quick test shows me that I can compile a kernel with this
value set to 65k and it works. I have not tried higher since I don't
understand what this limit refers to and what the dependencies are - I'm
just holding off rolling up my sleeves and following the variable in the
kernel).

Also this limit seems to be limited to ext3. My tests on my other hosts [UFS
(on my FreeBSD box), HFS (OSX), NTFS (WinXPPro), ZFS (FreeBSD)]  don't have
this limit, and I'm wondering why other FSs have been able to get around
this problem but not EXT3. Also, the EXT4 header file has the same limit (at
least according to ext4_fs.h).

I've done a bunch of google searches and I can't seem to find any reason why
this limit exists outside of historical space-saving (there was one
reference to the inode count being an int16).

With modern needs (specifically multimedia) these limits seem a bit archaic.
But I'm sure there are good reasons which I just don't know. Perhaps someone
could enlighten me, or at least help me go down the correct rabbit hole?

Cheers

On 4/18/08, Venkatraman S <venkat83@gmail.com> wrote:
> Well, yes - am really confused! And have no intentions of starting a flame
>  war - any personal experiences or useful links would be of immense help.
>
>  This is my first foray into web-development using Open Source frameworks and
>  tools and am just not able to decide on the course of action that i need to
>  take. I did have a brief stint with RoR and like it , but at the same time
>  TG seems to work fine with business layer (which is primarily in Python);
>  and I havent tried Django. I havent seen any actual web app written in any
>  of these(Tg/Django) experiencing a huge load and still remain stable. But it
>  looks like Guido van Rossum prefers Django (
>  http://www.artima.com/weblogs/viewpost.jsp?thread=158931 ).
>
>  # Am trying to build an app which will have millions of concurrent users and
>  is going to be highly distributed.

 None of the three frameworks will help you.
>  # It should scale really well and does not go astray when in use.

Too vague of a rrequirement. You need to tell us what exactly you are
doing then only we can suggest  about scalability. And yes i stil hate
teh word "scalable"
>  # I am comfortable with pragramming, but do not want to essentially take
>  care of low level programming(and hence i like Python's way).

 Comfortable with programing and building a large applications are two
different worlds (or galaxies as I would like to put in). Builiding,
deploying and maintaining large applications requires *lot* of
experiece, patience, an eye for detail and intelligence. Frameworks
normalyy fail to provide the kind of control you need to achieve the
goals.
>  # Cleaner integration with Ajax libs would be also required.
>  # Easy on the database (will be using a replicated/clustered MySQL), hence
>  an easy to use ORM

 Ajax, Mysql , ORM.... looks like you are more interested in building
a buzzword compliant language than an application which works.

>
>  Any 'sincere' advice or hints would be great :)

Ok I have following sincere advices

1) Requirements posted by you are too vague and you can only expect
vague replies. Given the current requirements posted even PHP can
fullfill your requirements.

2) Coming to frameworks you mentioned
 2.1) R0R :- provides you with speed, lots of libraries, completely
buzzword compliant and comes with lots of goodies. Overall one of the
most useless framework I have ever used. Gives you an illusion of
speed of development. Most of the applications Ihave seen developed
using R0R fail to match even the performance of J2EE. R0R eats (or I
shoudl say wastes) lot of resources and forget about distributed
applications.
 2.2) Django :- Very usefull framework when you have requirements
clearly defined. If your requriements or datamodel changes frequently
then not that great of a framework to touch upon. One of the best
frameworks around, if you are buliding application for mature
processes like that of Washington Post. Down side of django is the
over dependancy on ORM. Not only django uses a non standard ORM, it is
next to impposible to make that ORM talk to a distributed db. Another
problem with django might be load balancing, I am not sure if the
chilidish django webserver can handle load balancing. Overall, django
is good for cloased site and monolithic servers. :)
 2.3) TG :- So far so good. TG has some scaling issues reason being
the over dependancy on ORM and some wrong archietectural decisions.
TG is planing to move away fom cherrypy  and go to python paste as the
webserver, saying that porting to cherrypy3 is too much of work for
them. So in the migration to paste, I am sure TG will end up loosing
load balancing capabilities too.

3) Dude, do some research... What you are trying to achive cant be
achieved with one framework or one language. Be ready to use more than
one programing language.

4) Libraries are better than frameworks

5) Postgres is fast enough, standard compliant database, with 20 years
of development behind it.

6) Builiding your own platform is sometimes more useful than using OTSS.

7) Cherrypy 3 is good with load balancing, scales, works with any
database, any tempalting engine and any ORM. Allows lot of flexibility
by allowing you hooks for custom processing.

8) 99.9% ORMs are crap.

9) Ask for more...

regards
VK

On 19-Apr-08, at 12:26 PM, vivek khurana wrote:

>>> Another
>>> problem with django might be load balancing, I am not sure if the
>>> chilidish django webserver can handle load balancing.
>>>
>>
>>  the 'childish' django webserver is meant for development. As it  
>> can only
>> handle one user at a time, only an idiot will use it for production.
>> Production sites run on apache, lighty, nginx and what have you -  
>> load
>> balancing is done using memcached and perlbal.
>
>  hehe, do oyu need any other proof of lack of muscle pwer in django. A
> python powered app using a webserver written in perl (perlbal).

my friend, django is a web framework. It is not a web server. It is a  
web framework using LAMP stack. It is not a server. It uses as a  
database backend server, postgres, mysql, sqlite, oracle ... none of  
which are written in python. As webserver it can use apache, nginx,  
lighty - or all three of them, either alone or backed by memcached  
and/or perlbal - none of these are written in python. It uses html,  
css and javascript - again nothing to do with python. It also uses  
operating systems like Linux, *bsd, OSX and windows - again none of  
them written in python. Remember again it is a *framework* which is  
just to use all the elements of a LAMP stack in a more efficient  
manner. Of course, if you are writing a webapp that will only be used  
by one person at a time you can use the django run server which is  
written in python. It is totally flexible in that it can use  
practically any templating language and any ORM, including  
SQLAlchemy. And for version control it can use subversion or git or  
even mercurial (although that is in python). In fact for deployment I  
know a lot of people use that Rails thingie (forgot it's name)  
written in Ruby. And I am quite sure a lot of people also use puppet  
to configure and maintain their servers on which they run their  
django apps. And yes, there are people who use phppgadmin and  
phpmyadmin to look after the databases they run with django (shocking  
isnt it, a python application that uses php to maintain the rdbms!)

1) Going by your answer please differentiate between a "web framework"
and a library ? (and notice the word web here)

2) django provides a way to handle rdbms and people use phpmyadmin etc
instead of built in admin panel out of choice or ease. But django is
not dependednt on phpmyadmin (or any other php  application) to
provide basic services. Databases have native interfaces too which can
be used. OTOH perlbal is something django "needs" to ensure decent
availability (please see I haven't used hig-availability yet).

regards
VK

Hello,

I want to create a pxe-server.
This server will need to store 10 unique configurations for 10 different
machines. Let's say each configuration is in a separate directory on the
server.

I want each machine to pxe-boot from the pxe-server and get the
configuration from its unique directory from the server and accordingly

that part is fine.

When I have just one config stored on the server, everything is fine,
but cannot get the way for storing and reaching to a unique separate
configuration as per each machine.

Any pointers on how to do that ?

>>

oops, I did not notice this. This is pure BS. Django has absolutely  
*no* functionality for handling RDBMS. The django admin app is purely  
for entering data. The responsibility for creating and maintaining  
the rdbms lies with the administrator. Django will not create a  
database. Django will not vacuum it. Django will not finetune it.  
Django has some limited functionality for creating tables - but  
preserving the integrity of the data is purely in the hands of the db  
admin.

Same with apache - finetuning and tweaking of apache is again upto  
the admin. Django doesnt do it. Same with the OS - django will not  
tweak the OS.

From raamanp at yahoo.co.in  Sun Apr 20 06:19:26 2008
From: raamanp at yahoo.co.in (Raman.P)
Date: Sun Apr 20 06:19:39 2008
Subject: [Ilugc] pxe server for multiple machines to boot
In-Reply-To: <1208610834.3659.77.camel@laptop.censusindia.net>
Message-ID: <262338.49376.qm@web94603.mail.in2.yahoo.com>


--- On Sat, 19/4/08, Sudhir Gandotra <sudhir@openlx.com> wrote:

> Hello,
> 
> I want to create a pxe-server.
> This server will need to store 10 unique configurations for
> 10 different
> machines. Let's say each configuration is in a separate
> directory on the
> server.
> 
> I want each machine to pxe-boot from the pxe-server and get
> the
> configuration from its unique directory from the server and
> accordingly
> to get the configured and then the go for the data of the
> 
> When I have just one config stored on the server,
> everything is fine,
> but cannot get the way for storing and reaching to a unique
> separate
> configuration as per each machine.

You may have to look at dhcpd.conf file and tweak
a) option root-path : This tells the server and root file system
                      e.g pxeserver.com:/pxefiles/server1
b) option filename  : this gives the exact pxe file fetch by
                      the client.
                      e.g /tftpboot/pxelinux.0

These can be setup on per client basis using MAC address.

Raman.P

From siva.chandran.p at gmail.com  Sun Apr 20 11:41:07 2008
From: siva.chandran.p at gmail.com (Siva Chandran P)
Date: Sun Apr 20 11:41:21 2008
Subject: [Ilugc] 0 TermEmulator - A pure python module for V100 terminal
	emulation
Message-ID: <e3a31dcd0804192311l293c6d5dledeb642491985e3f@mail.gmail.com>

Hi,

I have written a python module for V100 terminal emulation namely
TermEmulator. It supports most of the important escape sequences, text
attributes(style, foreground and background color) and etc. A typical usage
would be capture the output of terminal program and send it to the module
then we can get the final emulated screen output.

For more information check out
http://sivachandran.blogspot.com/2008/04/termemulator-10-released.html and
you can get the module at http://www.sourceforge.net/projects/termemulator.

Siva Chandran P
sivachandran.blogspot.com

Subject: [Ilugc] Gurb installation problem ubuntu 7.10 with two hdds
Message-ID: <289b5e200804200926k57bacc82h111bb9a8c37065fb@mail.gmail.com>

Hi

I am having a system with 40 GB PATA HDD dual booting with windows xp and
Ubuntu 7.04 using grub installed in its mbr (hd0,0). Now I added a 160 gb
SATA drive and installed ubuntu 7.10 and windows xp in it. By oversight  I
choose the default options, and the grub is overwritten into the PATA disk.
Hence when I boot from the SATA HDD, only windows xp is available. My
intention is not distrub the PATA HDD and to use the BIOS settings to boot
