From thejaswi.puthraya at gmail.com  Mon Apr 21 07:18:01 2008
From: thejaswi.puthraya at gmail.com (Thejaswi Puthraya)
Date: Mon Apr 21 07:18:26 2008
Subject: [Ilugc] Re: Django, TG or Rails
Message-ID: <e49f53920804201848k4eefc1d4pe522f11e3808304f@mail.gmail.com>

I didn't want to get drawn into this discussion but now that I have
got in, I would like to make certain clarifications.

>  Thejaswi Puthraya wrote:
>  >>  > If you are planning to go for concurrent users and require transaction
>  >>  > support then
>  >>  > none of the three will fit your bill. And MySQL will not help your
>  >>  > situation.
>  >>  >
>  >>  >
>  >>  Your comment on MySQL is interesting - how did you arrive at this??
>  >
>  > MySQL is not ACID compliant. True it might support transactions lately
>  > through InnoDB but it still lags behind in features like Stored Procs,
>  > sub-queries, triggers etc.
>  >
>
>  ummm, http://forums.mysql.com/read.php?97,18003,18003

Recently while I was helping out my friend's company that works with
huge databases (the one that I helped him out was 1.5Gigs) that used
MySQL 5.0 with the MyISAM engine, I faced too many issues.

They use MyISAM engine because their work is based heavily on SELECTs
with very few INSERTs. MyISAM has only table-level locking and this
can be a problem occasionally(as I realized during the period). InnoDB
provides ACID-compliance and row-level locking but can be very very
very slow in such a situation.

>  w.r.t Sub-queries, which decade are you living in ?

2008 :) Just try using MySQL with subqueries and see the difference in
performance. While I was trying subqueries on that huge database, it
sometimes took hours for a sub-select to complete when it was taking
minutes as an individual select. So personally, this feature is almost
non-existent!!! Even for smaller databases of the order of 25,000
records, it was taking 8 to 9 seconds. Falcon seems to have a very
neat solution and am looking forward to using it soon.

All major ORMs support sub-queries and they are a real useful feature.
http://www.sqlalchemy.org/docs/04/sqlexpression.html#sql_everythingelse_correlated
http://www.sqlobject.org/SQLObject.html#subqueries-subselects

Infact, performance wise a sub-query is better than a join.

>  w.r.t triggers, yea - mysql does not have usable stable released code that does
>  do triggers. however, having said that - if you read the OP's email - he
>  mentioned a replicated clustered mysql instance for the backend db. Only crazy (
>  or very talented ? ) people use triggers in such an environment. Its very very
>  very hard to generate a sane db state if you do. You'll end up building so much
>  janitorial code that the whole point of doing a replicated multi head db will
>  come into question.

I personally love to off-load as much to the database than code it in
the web-app. It reduces the head-ache of coding that in your web-app.
Triggers play a very important role (esp in my case, and yes I am
neither crazy nor talented :). MySQL's triggers are still not upto the
level where they can really be useful. Haven't used clustered mysql
instance so can't talk about it.

I am looking forward to MySQL 6.0 which will make MySQL very
attractive. Till then, I am happy with Postgres.

Having built web-apps that deal with large data, I was just giving my
opinion. Before choosing any software esp for a corporates a thorough
study has to be done. A mailing list can only act as a guidance
(sometimes can also have adverse effect).

Forgive me if I any of my remarks have offended you :) And yes, I am
not going to get drawn further into this discussion.

-- 
Cheers
Thejaswi Puthraya
http://thejaswi.info/

Date: Mon Apr 21 11:38:28 2008
Subject: [Ilugc] Iptables in Debian etch
In-Reply-To: <5ef2113c0804202257ica4bb06ic3cbe873badf9878@mail.gmail.com>
References: <5ef2113c0804202257ica4bb06ic3cbe873badf9878@mail.gmail.com>

On Mon, Apr 21, 2008 at 11:27 AM, Senthil Kumaran S <stylesen@gmail.com> wrote:
> Hi,
>
>  I am using Debian etch and the default kernel which comes along with
>  it "2.6.18-6-686 #1 SMP". Can I use iptables directly with this kernel
>  or I need to recompile the kernel. How do I verify whether support for
>  iptables is enabled in my kernel?

# cat /boot/config-2.6.18-6-686 | grep -i netfilter

if the o/p lists CONFIG_NETFILTER=y ... then you  have iptables enabled...

and Debian Etch is having it enabled for standard installation...

From sbharathi at MidasComm.Com  Mon Apr 21 11:42:09 2008
From: sbharathi at MidasComm.Com (Bharathi Subramanian)
Date: Mon Apr 21 11:39:04 2008
Subject: [Ilugc] One Day One GNU/Linux Command (ALIAS)
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0804211120500.1155-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>

One Day One GNU/Linux Command
=============================

alias - Create alias name for a command.

Summary: 

alias is Bash build-in command. This is very useful to create a simple
alias for a complex/long/frequent commands. Once alias created, you
can use alias to call the original command. This alias are deleted
after closing the shell session. For the next session, you have create
it again. So to avoid this problem, you add it in your .bashrc file.

Example:

$ alias  -- Prints all alias commands

$ alias cls=clear -- Alias for new user from DOS world.

$ alias ls="ls -F --color=always" -- Alias long ls command.

$ alias mycd='cd a/b/c/d/e/f/h' -- Shortcut for long CD.

$ alias ls -- Print the alias' original command.

$ \ls -- Skip alias and run the original command.

Read: man bash or help alias

HTH :)
-- 
Bharathi S

From f2005180 at bits-pilani.ac.in  Mon Apr 21 11:43:58 2008
From: f2005180 at bits-pilani.ac.in (Karthik Ramgopal)
Date: Mon Apr 21 12:26:13 2008
Subject: [Ilugc] RE:Grub installation problem ubuntu 7.10 with two hdds
	(Dhanagopal R)
In-Reply-To: <20080421051159.407061DB294@www.ae.iitm.ac.in>
References: <20080421051159.407061DB294@www.ae.iitm.ac.in>
Message-ID: <000001c8a376$ebee71c0$c3cb5540$@ac.in>

Hi,
     You have 2 options.

1. Install GRUB to the MBR of your SATA disk

	a)Boot into the Gutsy Live CD
	b)Fire up a terminal and switch to a root shell, sudo -s
	c)grub-install /dev/sda

2. Change the option in your BIOS to boot from PATA
<You can find it in Hard disk Boot priority under Boot preferences in most
common BIOS setup programs>

Regards,
Karthik Ramgopal
BITS Pilani

Thejaswi Puthraya wrote:
>>  ummm, http://forums.mysql.com/read.php?97,18003,18003
> 
> Recently while I was helping out my friend's company that works with
> huge databases (the one that I helped him out was 1.5Gigs) that used
> MySQL 5.0 with the MyISAM engine, I faced too many issues.

so, you had issues because you did not know what you were doing ? I am 
responsible for a fair number of lage mysqldb installations ( large by mysql 
terms - in the region of 150 - 180 GB ), and dont have 'too many issues'.

> They use MyISAM engine because their work is based heavily on SELECTs
> with very few INSERTs

I dont see how that disqualifies innodb as an engine type ?

> MyISAM has only table-level locking and this
> can be a problem occasionally(as I realized during the period). InnoDB
> provides ACID-compliance and row-level locking but can be very very
> very slow in such a situation.

Thats fud. Innodb for larger sized db's can actually show massive performance 
improvements over myisam, even in read intensive situations. The fact that you 
can tune the innodb resources and index's is in itself a massive advantage 
because you can get it to behave in a manner most suited to your workload and data.

> 
>>  w.r.t Sub-queries, which decade are you living in ?
> 
> 2008 :) Just try using MySQL with subqueries and see the difference in
> performance. While I was trying subqueries on that huge database, it
> sometimes took hours for a sub-select to complete when it was taking
> minutes as an individual select. 

Sounds, to me, like a db schema not done right and/or no optimisation. I can run 
multiple levels of selects from either within proc or on the mysql cli with 
subsecond response times on large'ish db with no issues ( 180GB, in one db 300 
odd tables )

> Infact, performance wise a sub-query is better than a join.

rubbish. sub-q and joins have a small functional interset, you cant just 
generalise something like that.

> I personally love to off-load as much to the database than code it in
> the web-app. It reduces the head-ache of coding that in your web-app.
> Triggers play a very important role (esp in my case, and yes I am
> neither crazy nor talented :). MySQL's triggers are still not upto the
> level where they can really be useful. Haven't used clustered mysql
> instance so can't talk about it.
...
> Having built web-apps that deal with large data, I was just giving my
> opinion. 
...
> Forgive me if I any of my remarks have offended you :) And yes, I am
> not going to get drawn further into this discussion.

No, thats fine - your comments dont offend me, Its just that all your opinion 
and most of your comments are incorrect and based on the fact that you dont seem 
to either know much about mysql or use it. You are obviously a pgsql fan, and 
while that is fine - that should be no reason to slag off something else.

> Is there System Restore facility in RHEL 5..?

I have never tried RHEL, but if it does possess a rescue feature like
Fedora, then I guess it has to be either booting with a Rescue CD or
booting with the first CD with "linux rescue" at the boot prompt,
following which the detected system is mounted in /mnt/sysimage for
you to fix, either by fiddling around in it, or by chrooting in there
and running the commands you want.

HTH. I am not sure if this will work in RHEL, though.

From sbharathi at MidasComm.Com  Tue Apr 22 11:59:18 2008
From: sbharathi at MidasComm.Com (Bharathi Subramanian)
Date: Tue Apr 22 11:55:12 2008
Subject: [Ilugc] One Day One GNU/Linux Command (DATE)
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0804221119230.1153-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>

One Day One GNU/Linux Command
=============================

date -  Print/Set the system data and time 

Summary: 

date will print the time information in different formats 
and user can also make a custom formats using the options.

Example:

$ date -- Print the current date and time.

$ date --rfc -- Print the date in RFC-822 format.

$ date -u -- Print time in UTC format.

$ date -d '3year ago' -- Same date but 3 yrs ago.

$ date -d '3year' -- Same date but after 3 yrs.

$ date --date='2 days ago' -- Day before yesterday.

$ date --date='2 days' -- Day after tomorrow.

$ date --set='-10 minutes' -- Reduce 10m in current time and set.

$ date '+%b %_e %a %T %p %Z %Y' -- Current date in custom format.

Read : info date or man date

Bye :)
-- 
Bharathi S

http://qa.debian.org/developer.php?login=Varun+Hiremath

Apart from Debian I have been contributing to many open source projects:

1) I am author of open source project python-gastables: python modules
for compressible gas flow calculations: Homepage:
code.google.com/p/python-gastables

2) I am also author of Krickscore - KDE applet for cricket scores.
http://linux.softpedia.com/get/Desktop-Environment/KDE/krickscore-25612.shtml

Homepage: http://varun.travisbsd.org/krickscore.php

3) I have been contributing to Jajuk - Advanced Juke box project,
where I am working as a Developer and Debian package maintainer.
Homepage: http://jajuk.info/index.php/Main_Page

4) I am also currently maintaing pidgin-festival ( formerly knows as
festival-gaim). I rewrote festival-gaim to make it work with the new
pidgin API. Homepage: http://sourceforge.net/projects/pidgin-festival/

How does it feels to have two DDs from neighbouring rooms?

(Kumar Appaiah stays next to my room)

It is a big advantage having him next door because we get to learn a
lot from each other. Usually there is a lot of activity going on in
Debian, and it becomes very difficult to keep track of things; having
another DD next door really helps a lot to catch up with action.

Read More about Varun at
http://fci.wikia.com/wiki/Varun_Hiremath

Cheers
Praveen

From sbharathi at MidasComm.Com  Wed Apr 23 11:11:20 2008
From: sbharathi at MidasComm.Com (Bharathi Subramanian)
Date: Wed Apr 23 11:07:11 2008
Subject: [Ilugc] One Day One GNU/Linux Command (CAT)
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0804231041200.2637-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>

One Day One GNU/Linux Command
=============================

cat -- CATenate files and display

Summary: 

Cat will do following functions on the files: Displaying them,
Combining copies of them and Creating new ones.

Jargon File: Catenate is an obscure word meaning "to connect in a
series", which is what the "cat" command does to one or more files.

Examples:

$ cat File  -- Dump the file on screen.

$ cat File1 File2 File3 -- Concat File1,File2 & File3 and display.

$ cat > File -- Concat the STDIN to STDOUT and FILE. 
                Press Enter and Ctrl+D to exit.

$ cat - File - Concat STDIN and File to STDOUT.

$ cat -n File -- Show the File with number for each line.

$ cat -b File -- Show the File with number for non-blank lines.

$ cat -s File -- Squeeze multiple blank lines to single.

$ cat -A File -- Show the Non-Printable Chars also.

STDIN  - Standard Input  - Keyboard
STDOUT - Standard Output - Screen

Read: man cat / info cat

HTH :)
-- 
Bharathi S

nature of this building material gives it some qualities of commodities;
yet its generative nature is exceptional to traditional economic
constructs. It also inconveniences economic belief systems that anchor
their perspective in the work of business, government, or both.

From sbharathi at MidasComm.Com  Thu Apr 24 10:52:17 2008
From: sbharathi at MidasComm.Com (Bharathi Subramanian)
Date: Thu Apr 24 10:47:55 2008
Subject: [Ilugc] One Day One GNU/Linux Command (TAC)
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0804241042200.3914-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>

One Day One GNU/Linux Command
=============================

tac -- Concatenate and Print files in reverse order.

Summary:

`tac' copies each file to standard output, reversing the records
(lines by default) in each separately. It is doing the reverse
function of the CAT (TAC) command.

Example:

$ tac myfile -- Print the file (Line by Line) in reverse order.

$ tac -r -s '[^a-zA-z0-9\-]' myfile -- Print the file (Word by Word)  
                 in reverse order, by passing the Regular expression.

$ tac -r -s '.\|' myfile -- Print the file (Char by Char) in reverse 
                            order.

Read: man tac

HTH :)
--
Bharathi S

From parth.technofreak at gmail.com  Thu Apr 24 14:13:09 2008
From: parth.technofreak at gmail.com (Parthan SR)
Date: Thu Apr 24 14:13:38 2008
Subject: [Ilugc] Contributing back
In-Reply-To: <20080424065204.GC22378@imsc.res.in>
References: <5580629a0804232229g1ddbca7er34f6fdda9ab8c0ad@mail.gmail.com>
	<20080424065204.GC22378@imsc.res.in>
Message-ID: <4810481D.4010106@gmail.com>

Hi,
>> I have started contributing bug reports for xubuntu. But somehow,
>> doing that alone does not satisfy.
>>     
I really wonder what you mean by "contributing bug reports"? If you mean 
"filing bug reports" then it is not even a full first step contribution. 
Lot of people file bugs, but never file them good enough. A simple check 
would have shown them that similar bugs exist, may be even a fix is 
mentioned. We face a lot of duplicate bugs and a major chunk of bug 
squad's job goes in clearing the duplicates.

Secondly, filing a bug is not important if you are not following it up. 
If you file a bug and leave it, hoping some will look into it, then it 
might not just happen. Often additional information are asked and when 
the reported doesn't respond, it negates the entire purpose of filing 
bugs and eventually you bug becomes invalid without a response.

If you are already doing things right by checking existing bugs before 
filing one, providing as much information as possible, following your 
bugs, etc. then feel free to move to the next level and help out the bug 
squad. We really need more hands to handle bugs from our ever 
increasing  (in size) community. And of course, trying to fix issues and 
offer solutions is another level ;)

-- 
---
With Regards,

Parthan "technofreak"
<gpg>  2FF01026
<blog> http://blog.technofreak.in

From rajasuperman at gmail.com  Thu Apr 24 17:06:39 2008
From: rajasuperman at gmail.com (Raja Subramanian)
Date: Thu Apr 24 17:07:26 2008
Subject: [Ilugc] How to record skype chat?
In-Reply-To: <dd680c2b0804231121g4369dd73t978b68ee3bdc7d20@mail.gmail.com>
References: <dd680c2b0804231121g4369dd73t978b68ee3bdc7d20@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <92f9a9560804240436t51ea8aa5v327a90ec9ce33aea@mail.gmail.com>

On Wed, Apr 23, 2008 at 11:51 PM, Shrinivasan T <tshrinivasan@gmail.com> wrote:
> How to record the skype voice chat session in linux?

The Skype protocol was never published.  Many have tried reverse
engineering it, and have various levels of success.  Some Skype
plugins exist that can record calls, but most plugins are primarily
Windows only.  Check the plugins section of Skype.com.

A simple work around is to use audacity and grab everything coming
out/in of your speakers/mic.

- Raja
From techgurushankar at gmail.com  Thu Apr 24 17:27:28 2008
From: techgurushankar at gmail.com (Shankar Ganesh)
Date: Thu Apr 24 17:27:41 2008
Subject: [Ilugc] How to record skype chat?
In-Reply-To: <92f9a9560804240436t51ea8aa5v327a90ec9ce33aea@mail.gmail.com>
References: <dd680c2b0804231121g4369dd73t978b68ee3bdc7d20@mail.gmail.com>
	<92f9a9560804240436t51ea8aa5v327a90ec9ce33aea@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <a03262640804240457u52408163xa45023c0d945a075@mail.gmail.com>

> On Wed, Apr 23, 2008 at 11:51 PM, Shrinivasan T <tshrinivasan@gmail.com>
> wrote:
> How to record the skype voice chat session in linux?
>

Call Graph is a program that lets you record Skype calls. It's currently
available for Windows only, but there's a Linux version being developed.

http://callgraph.in/

If you're interested, you can request a preview version of the Linux version
by contacting them through this page: http://callgraph.in/contactus.php

Otherwise, you can use Audacity to record Skype calls. There's a guide over
here, but I'm not sure if the methods mentioned work:

http://blog.iamnotashamed.net/2006/03/31/5-steps-to-record-a-skype-call-with-audacity-free/

total was aroung 9GB. I am not sure what happen to the remaining 7GB. I
tried vmstat cmd and found that around 5.8GB was in inactive and 8.9GB
in active mode and only 720MB is free. 
 
What is the inactive memory and how to reclaim this memory.
 
[root@prod05 vm]# free -m
             total       used       free     shared    buffers

From sbharathi at MidasComm.Com  Fri Apr 25 10:12:38 2008
From: sbharathi at MidasComm.Com (Bharathi Subramanian)
Date: Fri Apr 25 10:07:49 2008
Subject: [Ilugc] One Day One GNU/Linux Command (NL)
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0804251001350.5554-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>

One Day One GNU/Linux Command
=============================

nl - Number lines of files

Summary:

Write each FILE to stdout, with line numbers added. With No FILE 
or -, read from stdin.

Examples :

$ nl myfile -- Writes all non-empty lines with number.

$ nl -ba myfile -- Number all lines.

$ nl -ba -l2 myfile -- Count 2 empty line as 1 and display

$ nl -nln myfile -- Numbers are left justified.

$ nl -nrz myfile -- Numbers are right justified and leading zeros

$ nl -w2 myfile -- Uses 2 column for the line number.

$ nl -s"> " myfile -- Insert "> " in between number and line.

$ nl -bp"^" myfile -- Number lines start with char 'T'.

$ ls | nl -- ls Output with line numbers

Read: man nl

HTH :)
-- 
Bharathi S

Message-ID: <20080425045524.GB12644@imsc.res.in>

On Fri, 25 Apr 2008, Siva Prakash wrote:
> It mean like a User 1 granting User 2, the right to send email as User 1.
> 
> When a User on vacation and he wants some other user to monitor his
> messages.

These two are not the same thing:
 a. Send a mail as someone else (SMTP Auth)
 b. Read mail sent to someone else (IMAP Auth)

As far as I know mail servers like exim4/postfix for SMTP
and dovecot/cyrus for IMAP support SASL for Authentication.

SASL authentication allows user A to be authenticated and then
authorized as user B. 

You can think of it like "sudo" where user A gives user A's password
to sudo and is thus permitted to do some work as user B (usually B is
root!).

I can't help you more since I have never used SASL myself! :-(

Regards,

Kapil.
--

On 25-Apr-08, at 5:04 PM, Thanigairajan murugan wrote:

> Hi Luggies,
>
> Is it possible to  access externally two web servers which are  
> running different nodes behind the firewall ?
>
> I am using shorewall.In this I can DNAT only one webserver,
> For this the code is as follows,
> DNAT       net   loc:192.168.0.20:80  tcp     80
> DNAT net      loc:192.168.0.20 tcp     www
You will need to use one port per web server
> To access the webserver which is running on other node (192.168.0.1),
>
> I tried as  follows
> DNAT       net   loc:192.168.0.1-192.168.0.20:80  tcp     80
> DNAT     net      loc:192.168.0.1-192.168.0.20 tcp     www
> but in vain.
Will not work unless you've DNAT round robin/ load balancing. Some  
routers support this. However, this assumes all webservers are running  
the same site else one would get sites at random.
> I also tried with one webserver's port as 81
> For this the code is as follows,
> DNAT       net   loc:192.168.0.1:81  tcp     80
DNAT net loc:192.168.0.1:80 tcp 81
This will redirect all calls on port 81 on the public side to port 80  
on the .1 server. The user must give the url http://host.domain:81

Mohan

Date: Fri Apr 25 19:08:06 2008
Subject: [Ilugc] Memory utilization issue
In-Reply-To: <7EBC04A2ECAE6F4C89159D294B69557403AC8725@CORP-HYD-MBX04.ENTCORP.TTSL.COM>
References: <7EBC04A2ECAE6F4C89159D294B69557403AC821F@CORP-HYD-MBX04.ENTCORP.TTSL.COM>
	<A70864EE-92BF-4FCE-9382-BCBB1646D488@thenilgiris.com>
	<7EBC04A2ECAE6F4C89159D294B69557403AC8725@CORP-HYD-MBX04.ENTCORP.TTSL.COM>
Message-ID: <92f9a9560804250637v5b8fac67i5ac6281a8b9775e7@mail.gmail.com>

On Fri, Apr 25, 2008 at 10:19 AM, Anandh Gurusamy
<Anandh.Gurusamy@tatatel.co.in> wrote:
> Nop, the performance of the machine is normal, but we are unable to
>  install the application as it check for avaiable free memory.

Check contents of /proc/sys/vm/min_free_kbytes.  This file
lists the size of "free" memory the system must always preserve
in case RAM is needed urgently (think device driver buffers).

Setting it to a higher value will "free" up more RAM so you
can install your application.  Eg. to free up 2G of RAM use:

echo `expr 2048 \* 1024` > /proc/sys/vm/min_free_kbytes

Do **not** make this setting permanent on a production box.

Do **not** set a very high value for this setting as it may cause
out of memory errors and kill running processes (esp mysql).

Needless to say, don't run this on a production box without
careful analysis.


Unused memory is wasted memory, so Linux uses nearly all
unused memory to buffer various things (files, VM pages, etc).
The kernel automatically reduces the size of the buffer cache
whenever applications require additional RAM.  A few MB of
memory is typically kept free to ensure that urgent demands
of RAM by device drivers during DMA operations, etc can
be serviced immediately.

See the contents of /proc/sys/vm/* for how you can tune your
VM behavior.


This test for free memory in your application installer is legacy
behavior and will fail on nearly all modern OSes.  It's time
to file this as a bug report with your software vendor.

- Raja

--- On Fri, 25/4/08, senthilraja P <technocraze@gmail.com> wrote:

> 
> I was considering such FOSS lab in my village.  We ran a
> computer shop 10
> years before, and we now have around 3-4 P2 PC's.
>

> 
>    the old pc contained 3 PCI slot, and hence the person
> told, we can create
> three thin client machines, with one old PC and 3 monitors
> using that PCI
> card.
>
In linux this is called multi-seat. Put PCI-VGA card for monitor out, add usb keyboard and mouse for every additional set. No special hardware is required.

However, on old hardware performance may not be good.
 
> Now i have the following question?
> 1. If we are buying new machines, why should we go for Thin
> client, as
> hard-disk costs only 2000 now.
It is not only hard-disk cost. If you setup LTSP(Linux Terminal server project), the benefits are
a) No hdd cost
b) Low power cpu on clients - celereon
c) If pxe booting is supported by mother board, no need for
    cd drive, fdd etc
d) Less maintenance, HDD, cd-rom failure are very common
e) Less RAM on client
But you need one decent PC with atleast 512MB of RAM.

> 2. IF we go for thin client, do we need any special
> hardware apart from the
> PC's?
With ltsp you don't need anything special.
> 3. Is it really possible to establish thin client by sing
> the PCI card?
> 4. Is it possible to setup three thin clients, in the same
> PC?
> 
Yes, it is called multi-seat in linux.

I am using a P-100 purchased in 1997 as thin client even today.

For more details look at ltsp.org, multi-seat page in wikipedia.org

Raman.P

From prem at songbirdtech.com  Sat Apr 26 09:51:07 2008
From: prem at songbirdtech.com (Prem Kurian Philip)
Date: Sat Apr 26 09:51:25 2008
Subject: [Ilugc] C3 - Update for the week
In-Reply-To: <20080425213541.3619E1DB266@www.ae.iitm.ac.in>
References: <20080425213541.3619E1DB266@www.ae.iitm.ac.in>
Message-ID: <49233.61.247.255.57.1209183667.squirrel@www.songbirdtech.com>

From: "senthilraja P" <technocraze@gmail.com>

> I had an interesting experience to share.  i was very enthusiastic and
> proposed setting a computer center for the labourer's nearby.  But the
> sponsors raised the following question.
>
> 1. The purpose of the training center is to make the people employeable.
> Will training on open source source softwares like openoffice create any
> employment for them?
> 2. They are not going to learn technical stuf.. They will learn what is
> required in the market..
>
>
> I have no answer for this, as i am sure, none of the business offices use
> open source softwares.
>
> Just wanted to share with you all.

Speaking from my experience as running a company, it is very, very
unlikely that I will consider anyone for a job just because they know
openoffice. There are literally thousands of unemployed degree holders out
there who are always applying for work.

I am not trying to discourage you, but you should perhaps think a bit more
about the type of work that you are preparing these people for. I have
done a bit on my own along similar lines and therefore I include my
thoughts below:

You need to decide what type of jobs you are going to be preparing these
people for. If it is secretarial type of work, then you need to teach
them:

a) English - most places will require this
b) How to answer the phone professionally
c) How to welcome people in the office and behave professionally in an
office environment
d) How to dress professionally
e) Handle people coming in for appointments or seeking appointments etc..
f) How to write a professional letter
g) Usage of fax, email, usage of yellow pages etc
h) Fast typing
i) Basic accounting
j) How to find information on the web
k) .... and many more.

Knowledge of openoffice or MSOffice will be essential but you will need to
see this within the context of all the responsibilities a job like this
would entail. Preparing someone to use a computer is only a very small
part of the job.

Also, it really helps to have these labourers join an open university to
start on some degree as most places these days will require that. Also, it
will help if someone can start a bank account in their name for them so
that they can get used to using a bank account, an ATM card, saving money
etc.

It is a real uphill battle for the poor to join the mainstream. They will
need all the help they can get. I thank you for starting this initiative.

Regards,
PK

> In nutshell the otherguy gets the full copy of the mail where
> as the first person only gets a part of the mail body.
> 
> Is there any way to accomplish this task. The work around is sending

the person who is supposed see that part.

The other person may object to your filling the mail with unreadable
junk.

Subject: [Ilugc] remove mandrake and install ubuntu

--- On Sat, 26/4/08, Raju s <rajusns@gmail.com> wrote:
> > did you try with Ubuntu CD?
> >
> > I want to try with Ubuntu.
> Shall i delete the partion where mandrake is installed?
> Will it be removed from the boot loader or how to remove it
> after
> installation.
If /boot is a separate partition then you have to delete it also.

You can install by choosing the partition on which mandrake was installed - in which case you need not delete. If /boot is separate and if you didn't remove it you may have to edit menu.lst file of grub - /boot/grub/menu.lst to remove mandrake entries.

From technocraze at gmail.com  Sat Apr 26 23:37:19 2008
From: technocraze at gmail.com (senthilraja P)
Date: Sat Apr 26 23:37:29 2008
Subject: [Ilugc] Bringing FLOSS to Everyday Academic Life
Message-ID: <c9ea6e770804261107y2a6b443dgb3522a6d47d668f2@mail.gmail.com>

Hi,

I had this idea of Bringing FLOSS software to every day life of colleges.

Most of the engineering colleges dont even have a mail server, and there are
not proper IT staff to guide the college management.

When some of my cousins recently approached me for some academic project, i
was little bit confused, on how to guide them.  They dont know even what a
web server was..

So, i enquired about some details like, individual computers for their
staff,  mail servers, Internet connection etc.

I proposed some very simple projects to them, which i have listed below.

1. Setup a mail server, and configure the mail client to use it.  Then
demonstrate to college management, and finally setup this for them to use.

2. Use blogs (wordpress) for college communication, from principals &
HOD's.  Blogs is a powerful medium, and important announcements, circulars,
communications can be posted on the internal blogs.

3. To setup a Wiki, to manage information, and documents.  (Media wiki is
under consideration as of now).  This will act as a central place for all
informations, like department schedules, syllabus, subject contents etc.
Any information could be managed in wiki.  Usage is limited to imagination.

4. An online course management software.

The purpose behind is to make the academic people to realise how FLOSS
softwares can be used in their daily life to easily manage things.
Once they tasted the benefits of these softwares, then there will be more
curiosity to manage other activities through intranet.

For example, issue management, leave management, etc.  The students will
have the practical knowledge of these softwares.

This would ultimately empower both the staffs and students to customize
these softwares to their requiremnts.

The motto is that only if we bring FLOSS to daily use, not only in personal
life, but in our work and academic environment, we would have the inherent
vision to further take it to next level.

By next level, i mean, setting up data centr, taking up internal project
using the students etc.

Imagine, if atleast half of the colleges can setup data centre, it will
usher a new wave of IT revolution..

Note:
Since its exam time, i could not start this initiative.  Once its over by
mid of may, i will start teaching them the basics of FLOSS, and train them
in technologis like Apache configuration, MySQL, PHP etc, that they would
practically put in to use.  I thought of going for java j2ee, but, i
thought, when they dont even know what a webserver is, it would be difficult
for them to grasp higher concepts.  So, PHP would be simple and good start
for them.

Depending on the outcome, i plan to form a team in their colleges,
comprising of students from 2nd year to final year, so that any project they
take, would have the continuity, as new batches would join, when the final
year batches go out.

Please share your opinions on this.

Regards,
Senthil Raja

Subject: [Ilugc] Bringing FLOSS to Everyday Academic Life

Hi,
>
>I had this idea of Bringing FLOSS software to every day life of colleges.
>
>Most of the engineering colleges dont even have a mail server, and there are
>not proper IT staff to guide the college management.

Our Engineering colleges are not like companies/industries to get advice/support from a IT staff.  The
colleges IT infrastructure is almost maintained or in control of IT vendors / suppliers who don't
let anything to be installed apart from the regularly used copyright softwares 
(This is the every day life of colleges I am seeing in the engineering colleges).

>

>When some of my cousins recently approached me for some academic project, i
>was little bit confused, on how to guide them.  They dont know even what a
>web server was..
>

My experience with engineering college students was even worse, many of them have never seen
Linux GUI desktop at all and almost all of them have used linux in their colleges in one of their Semesters.  

This is how they use Linux in colleges.  

Boot using M$ Windows OS -> Run Telnet <ip> -> Connect to Linux Server -> Get Black Window -> Open Vi Editor -> Compile using cc -> Run Linux Programs = Linux in Engineering College Labs).

What they all know about in Linux?

* A Windows machine with Telnet command is required to connect a Linux server
* Login with given user name and password
* Get into some shell (not worried whether it is /bash or /sh)
* Open Vi editor
* Use cc to compile the `C' program (look, not gcc)
* Execute and see the output of the program

This is the situation at present we can see in many engineering colleges how the students have been using Linux.

>So, i enquired about some details like, individual computers for their

All the above ideas looks really great, but practically it would be very hard to 
explain these things to college managementt and make use of these FOSS tools for effective use.

In the past recent months, I have started discussing with few Engg. college HODs, Principal, Secretary,
Directors, Chairman and Management people about the importance of emerging FOSS technologies and its
wider usage in industries and governments increasing day-by-day and if academia fails to implements these things
in education, then a wider gap would exist between Academic and Industry.  After long and 
strong discussions  I have got some positive reponses from them.  Now few engineering colleges have
accepted our proposal to setup a complete Free / Open Source Software Lab (we have already setup 2 labs in Polytechnics this April) which could be used by students/staffs effectively in learning the new FOSS technologies in time.

We are looking for similar minded people who can join in our initiative to promote FOSS in education.

Regards

Baskar

Hello,

On Sun, 27 Apr 2008, support@linuxpertacademy.com wrote:
> Our Engineering colleges are not like companies/industries to get
> advice/support from a IT staff.

Why do they need support from outside? Most academic places where
GNU/Linux is extensively deployed depend on the competence of their
own staff.

Here are two possible reasons why they depend on external sources:
 a. The academic people are not interested. They see no added value
    from learning about managing systems.
 b. The students are not trusted by the authorities to help with the
    IT infrastructure.
The LUG can do very little about (b) but it will help if we can do
educate people about the value of learning about systems.

> The colleges IT infrastructure is almost maintained or in control of
> IT vendors / suppliers who don't let anything to be installed apart
> from the regularly used copyright softwares

Which is not to say that they are very competent with the proprietary
software packages which they install! 

> Boot using M$ Windows OS -> Run Telnet <ip> -> Connect to Linux
> Server -> Get Black Window -> Open Vi Editor -> Compile using cc ->
> Run Linux Programs = Linux in Engineering College Labs).

Hey! Don't knock this method of learning. I learnt things this
way. Except that I used DOS rather than Windows. In those days most
machines were XT's and could only act as dumb terminals to the *one*
386 we had running GNU/Linux. (Yes! I am that old!)

I think the original poster's ideas are good as long as they don't
forget the hands-on instructional component.

Even in IMSc, which is virtually a complete GNU/Linux environment, we
continually face pressure to "let the vendors handle it" and we know
what that means.

Regards,

Kapil.

Strong affinity towards a change in use of computer

[snip]...
> Once its over by
> mid of may, i will start teaching them the basics of
> FLOSS, and train them
> in technologis like Apache configuration, MySQL, PHP
> etc, that they would
> practically put in to use.  I thought of going for
> java j2ee, but, i
> thought, when they dont even know what a webserver

> simple and good start

A lot of whom I have met in the FOSS community (not
many) recommend Python over most other languages.
Python tends to enforce some standard practices
(comments, indentation, etc.) and therefore, is
probably considered to be good for beginners. However,
I have been used to the typical (if so-called)
learning of C -> C++ and then to Java. 

(Though I don't really think about C++ after being
into Java; and C is something, that I usually
recommend, though it may not be suitable for
beginners)

> Please share your opinions on this.

I would like to add a case study (not significant
enough, though) which I consider a small achievement. 

Our course content demanded that practical be
conducted using the GCC compiler, along with a custom
supplied Library (called shmlib.h) for Parallel
Programming, typically illustrating Shared Memory
Programming. 

I managed to pull in a few guys to get started (since
we did not have instructors for the practical
sessions) with programming under a Linux distribution.
Unfortunately, we didn't have machines installed with
a distro. I had to request my course co-ordinator to
install some Linux distribution so that we could
begin. Some were configured without the X-window
system, and some were with the X-window system (more
aplty, X.org). Though I thought of recommending
K/Ubuntu, I knew most of them don't come pre-installed
with GCC, and acquiring an internet connection on a
computer was more difficult, since most mis-use
bandwidth.

When a few of us managed to start programming, other
students (who were /supposed/ to perform the
practical) also joined us. My course co-ordinator
noticed this, and asked me if I wanted more computers
installed with Linux distributions for practising. 

Later, we had a mini-lab setup with four computers
(without internet, for obvious reasons) with Mandriva
Linux 10.1 with KDE 3.3.x and ICEWM setup as window
managers / DE. 

In short, it is almost like a 60-40 of investment of
resources from students-collegestaff to take FLOSS to
the next level.

I assume, NRCFOSS has done quite a bit in Chennai,
West Bengal and Rajasthan for introducing FLOSS in
academics. You might want to co-ordinate and help them
in their efforts.

From kapil at imsc.res.in  Mon Apr 28 06:45:47 2008
From: kapil at imsc.res.in (Kapil Hari Paranjape)
Date: Mon Apr 28 06:46:21 2008
Subject: [Ilugc] xwindows applications through putty?
In-Reply-To: <Pine.LNX.4.58.0804271630050.8150@chi.spunge.org>
References: <Pine.LNX.4.58.0804271630050.8150@chi.spunge.org>
Message-ID: <20080428011545.GA19390@imsc.res.in>

Hello,

On Sun, 27 Apr 2008, carti wrote:
> The question is,
> Through putty(using X11-forwading option) can I access the x-applications
> in the Linux server(without additional softwares)?. This will I be able to
> do, without any additional software like hummingbird or x-manager like applications.?

You need to have some kind of X server running on your Windows
machine if you want to run X applications remotely.

Here is an alternative approach.

1. Start a vncserver on the GNU/Linux side. This will give you
   a port number like 59xx in its output. 

   This is a virtual X server which "draws" to memory and outputs
   this drawing to port 59xx. It also accepts vncevents over the port
   and converts them to Xevents for the server.

2. use putty to connect to the GNU/Linux machine and forward 
   a port something like
   	local port: 5901
   	remotehost: localhost (this is localhost at the remote end!)
   	remoteport: 59xx (same as above) 

   This is just a tunnel connecting your machine to the GNU/Linux
   machine. This step is only required for security of the data
   being sent.

3. Download and install a vnc viewer for windows and start it. When
   it prompts for a port and host give 5901 and localhost.

   The viewer takes the data coming from this port and draws it. It
   also converts local keyboard and mouse activity to vncevents and
   sends them over the port.

This should work reasonably though it may feel like watching a badly
recorded VCD at times.

Regards,

Kapil.
--

can maintain a "MicroSoft solution for mailserver" *properly* but

can only fix punctures on Fiats and not Ambassadors! (I use that

Linux *used to* require more work than the click-clack-cluck under MS.

read/understand/edit configuration files?!

Apparently most IIT students are also no longer interested in
"hacking" (as in tinkering with computers), they just want the latest
video game/mobile gadget and be cool! Ah, the good old days! (/me ducks) ;-)

From sbharathi at MidasComm.Com  Mon Apr 28 10:38:12 2008
From: sbharathi at MidasComm.Com (Bharathi Subramanian)
Date: Mon Apr 28 10:33:20 2008
Subject: [Ilugc] One Day One GNU/Linux Command (WATCH)
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0804281021240.1099-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>

One Day One GNU/Linux Command
=============================

watch - Periodically run and show the output of a Program

Summary:

Watch runs the specified command(s) repeatedly, displaying its output.
This allows us to monitor the output changes over time. Press Ctrl+C
to stop the Watch Command.

Examples :-

$ watch ls -- Every 2sec(default time) 'ls' is executed and output 
              is showed on the screen.

$ watch -n 6 who -- Every 6Sec 'who' run and list the current users

$ watch -d date -- Highlight the difference b/w successive updates

$ watch /sbin/ifconfig eth0 -- Watch the traffic on eth0 interface.

$ watch "/sbin/ifconfig eth0 | grep bytes" -- Watch RX/TX bytes.

$ watch "/sbin/ifconfig; date" -- Watch multiple commands.

Read: man watch

HTH :)
-- 
Bharathi S

On Mon, 28 Apr 2008, Kumar Appaiah wrote:
> though most people use GMail addresses.

This is the trend. No one sets up their own data services anymore.

	Mail server	GMAIL et al.
	Web server	Myspace et al.
	Blog		blogspot et al.
	Documents	Google docs et al.
	Software	Sourceforge, Alioth, et al.
	....
	Life		Second Life
(OK! So the last is a joke. :-))

It is not clear that this is necessarily a bad thing from the point
of view of wide adoption of FLOSS.

After all, if this is all that people need from the computer, then any
networked device will do just fine, so embedded devices with Linux
under the hood will do just fine. Look at the success of the EEE Pc.

However, it may[*] be bad from the point of view of getting people to
start thinking (about what goes on) inside their boxes.

It is also bad from the point of view that people should have *more*
control over their own data in order to be free.

Regards,

Kapil.

[*] I say "may" because, one can explore an EEE Pc without voiding
its warranty --- quite unlike an iPhone!
--

From ajitk at email.com  Tue Apr 29 00:24:56 2008
From: ajitk at email.com (Ajit Natarajan)
Date: Tue Apr 29 00:25:06 2008
Subject: [Ilugc] Re: Linux speech -> text
In-Reply-To: <20080428134323.D6F651DB26A@www.ae.iitm.ac.in>
References: <20080428134323.D6F651DB26A@www.ae.iitm.ac.in>
Message-ID: <48161D80.50805@email.com>

deva free wrote:
 > For commercial apps, you may consider LumenVox, they are reputed to 
be > good. i myself am going to get a few licenses from them very soon.

It doesn't look like Lumenvox would work for what I want to do. 
Dictation is specifically called out as not optimized.

http://www.lumenvox.com/resources/tips/HowLVsoftwareUsed.aspx

Now, let?s discuss the applications that LumenVox speech technology is 
not optimized for:

Dictation Software

Dictation software allows a user to speak or ?dictate? text directly 
into an application (ex. Microsoft Word, etc.). Often times the voice 
input is through a microphone connected to a PC, but sometimes dictation 
applications can occur via the telephone.

One common use of dictation software is medical transcription. Doctors, 
nurses and medical personnel can dictate their notes and have them 
transcribed using speech recognition technology into text. This removes 
the need of a human transcriber, and saves time and money for a doctor?s 
office. This software also addresses the ?bad handwriting? liability 
that many medical personnel face.

Dictation software improves in accuracy by having a trained user and 
also after ?learning? the user?s voice and pronunciations of certain words.

Desktop Software

This type of software enables PC users to navigate their computer by 
using their voice, instead of the keyboard. This software can be 
especially useful for the blind or people with repetitive strain 
injuries that prevent them from using a keyboard. However, anyone can 
use this software, as speech truly is the most natural interface for 
many useful devices.

Ajit

From sbharathi at MidasComm.Com  Tue Apr 29 12:02:17 2008
From: sbharathi at MidasComm.Com (Bharathi Subramanian)
Date: Tue Apr 29 12:16:46 2008
Subject: [Ilugc] One Day One GNU/Linux Command (FREE)
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0804291123120.3063-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>

One Day One GNU/Linux Command
=============================

free -- Display the memory utilization info.

Summary:

Displays the total amount of free and used physical memory and swap
space in the system, as well as the buffers & cache consumed by the
kernel.

Examples:

$ free -- Display the mem info in KB.

$ free -m -- Display the mem info in MB.

$ free -m -t -- Display the total mem info.

$ free -s 2 -- Display the mem info for every 2Sec.

$ free -s 2 -c 5 -- Display mem info for every 2Sec but only 5 times.

$ cat /proc/meminfo -- This is the original info which is used by free
                       command for the report.

Read: man free

Bye :)
-- 
Bharathi S

From sbharathi at MidasComm.Com  Wed Apr 30 11:17:01 2008
From: sbharathi at MidasComm.Com (Bharathi Subramanian)
Date: Wed Apr 30 11:11:29 2008
Subject: [Ilugc] One Day One GNU/Linux Command (DF)
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0804301055360.4920-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>

One Day One GNU/Linux Command 
=============================

df -- Disk Free and usage report

Summary:

df shows the amount of disk space available on the file-system (FS)
containing each file name argument. If no file name is given, then
the usage info of all currently mounted FSs are shown.

Examples:

$ df -- Usage report of all mounted FS.

$ df -P -- Output in POSIX format (Compare with previous output).

$ df -Th -- Show the partition type and size is in human readable
            format.

$ df -l -- Show only the local FS. No NFS, SMB

$ df -x tmpfs -- Don't list the 'tmpfs' partitions.

$ df -t nfs -- List only the 'nfs' partitions.

$ df /home -- Usage report of Home partition.

$ df /dev/hda1 -- Usage report of /dev/hda1

$ df myfile -- Display usage report of FS, which contain the myfile.

Read: man df

HTH :)
-- 
Bharathi S

Message-ID: <20080430064929.GC8420@imsc.res.in>

Hello,

On Wed, 30 Apr 2008, Venkatraman S wrote:
> Also,  a slight variant of "df /home" :
> df -h `pwd`

Note that "df /mountpoint" and "df /mountpoint/subdir"
will always give the same output since "df" is for "disk free"
and not "disk usage". If you want to know actual usage of 
/mountpoit/subdir you should use "du /mountpoint/subdir"

Kapil.
--

Can you explain a bit about the inactive memory in "vmstat -a -S M"
output. Why should the OS keep it inactive. When the application usage
itself is only 2GB what is the OS doing with the remaining memory.

Any suggestions on fixing the issue.

On Fri, Apr 25, 2008 at 10:19 AM, Anandh Gurusamy
<Anandh.Gurusamy@tatatel.co.in> wrote:
> Nop, the performance of the machine is normal, but we are unable to  
> install the application as it check for avaiable free memory.

Check contents of /proc/sys/vm/min_free_kbytes.  This file lists the
size of "free" memory the system must always preserve in case RAM is
needed urgently (think device driver buffers).

Setting it to a higher value will "free" up more RAM so you can install
your application.  Eg. to free up 2G of RAM use:

echo `expr 2048 \* 1024` > /proc/sys/vm/min_free_kbytes
